25th State Council Meeting of the Executive Yuan 79

Approved Zhejiang to Issue Debt Clearance Bonds

Hankou Municipality Reorganized Under Provincial Government

Appointment of Ma Hongkui as Chairman of Ningxia

The Executive Yuan held its 25th State Council meeting on the morning of the 9th.

Page 8

Attendees: Chiang Kai-shek, Liu Juiheng, Wang Zhengting, Liu Shangqing, Kong Xiangxi, Ma Fuxiang, Wang Boqun. Observers: Chen Shaokuan, Chen Yi, Li Shuhua. Chairman: Chiang Kai-shek. The resolutions were announced as follows: (1) The Zhejiang Provincial Government submitted a report stating that Zhejiang Province is experiencing financial difficulties and has significant arrears. It is proposed to issue Zhejiang Province Republic of China Year 20 Debt Clearance Bonds of 8 million yuan, specifically for clearing various arrears. The draft regulations have been prepared and submitted for review and approval. The resolution was passed and sent to the Legislative Yuan. (2) The Hubei Provincial Government telegraphed on the 31st of last month stating that the reorganization of the provincial and municipal governments is about to be completed. However, Hankou Municipality was originally planned to be changed from a special municipality to an ordinary municipality, but after soliciting opinions from all sectors in Wuhan, it was unanimously agreed that there is no need to establish a municipal government in Hankou. Those in charge of the business community are particularly firm. It is now proposed not to establish a municipality for the time being, but only to organize a municipal committee affiliated with the provincial government to specifically handle the municipal administration of Hankou. The establishment of a municipality will be considered when finances are sufficient and the municipal administration is developed. Please issue an order to cancel the current order to facilitate the completion of the process. Is this appropriate? Please telegraph instructions for compliance. The resolution was passed to change Hankou to a municipality affiliated with the provincial government and submitted to the National Government for promulgation. (3) Minister Kong proposed that there are many stone statues of Buddhas and figures in the caves of Tianlong Mountain in Taiyuan, Shanxi, which are carved into concave shapes on the stone walls and are massive creations from the prosperous period of the Northern Wei Tuoba clan. Recently, due to inadequate protection, there have been frequent cases of theft, sale, or damage. Even the stone roof of the cave has been seized by antique dealers with violence. It is proposed to order the local officials in Shanxi to provide effective protection to prevent further losses and to strictly investigate and order the return of those that have been stolen. Other provinces and cities also experience similar cases of damage to antiquities from time to time. It is also requested that the local governments of all provinces and cities be notified to take measures to preserve all antiquities within their borders and to strictly investigate and punish those who privately transport them, thereby maintaining the historical sites. Is this appropriate for resolution? The resolution was approved and submitted to the National Government to implement the promulgated Law on the Preservation of Antiquities from June 15th of this year and to order the Ministries of Interior and Education to properly formulate measures for implementation of preservation and return of antiquities and circulate them to the provincial and municipal governments for effective implementation. (4) The Ministry of Industry submitted the organization charter of the Commodity Inspection Bureau for review and record. The resolution was passed and submitted to the National Government for record. (5) The Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Finance jointly reported that Article 9 of the Republic of China Year 20 Jiangzhe Silk Industry Public Bond Regulations contains the term "special tax". Now that the special consumption tax has been suspended, the name of this special tax should be revised. This is respectfully submitted for review and amendment. The resolution was passed and sent to the Legislative Yuan. (6) It was resolved to appoint Ma Hongkui as Chairman of the Ningxia Provincial Government. (7) Zhang Daofan, member of the Zhejiang Provincial Government and concurrently Director of the Education Department, submitted a request to resign. The resolution was to retain him. (8) It was resolved that Li Zhonggong, member of the Anhui Provincial Government and concurrently Director of the Education Department, submitted a request to resign. The resolution was to retain him. Before he takes office, Commissioner Yu Enbo will be temporarily appointed as acting director. (9) It was discussed that the vacancy left by Jin Tao, Senior Engineer of the Ministry of Railways, being appointed to another position should be filled by promoting Zhu Baofen, Recommended Engineer.

A Declaration by Japan's Overseas Comrades Association, Truly Astonishing 80

Deliberating on Emergency Countermeasures Against China

Advocating a Hardening of Stance on Railway Issues

Our Compatriots Should Pay Close Attention

Shenyang Correspondence: The Japanese, due to their small land and large population, have long harbored desires to invade China to fulfill their colonial ambitions. Currently, as our nation engages with various countries to revise unequal treaties, Japan is vehemently opposing it.

They have now united officials and civilians to establish the Overseas Comrades Association, issuing a declaration to oppose our nation's treaty abolition. Their advocacy for a hardened stance on the Manchurian-Mongolian railway issue is particularly noteworthy. The named initiators of the Overseas Comrades Association include thirty-two prominent figures from Japanese political and social circles, such as Duke Sanetaka Ichijo, Baron Norikiyo Kami, and Narimoto Ohaba. The sponsors include one hundred and fifteen individuals such as Baron Kaneko Yudo. Shenyang has recently received the original text of the declaration issued by the association from Tokyo. We urge all compatriots not to dismiss it as mere bluster.

Regarding the Manchurian-Mongolian railway issue, China is currently employing two means to pressure the South Manchuria Railway (SMR): (1) disregarding past precedents and thoroughly engaging in low-price competition to reduce freight rates, and (2) implementing plans to encircle the SMR. Their intention is to diminish the economic value of the SMR and dampen our nation's enthusiasm for maintaining the SMR, as a clear strategy for reclaiming it in the future. At this juncture, if we do not make a resolute decision to shatter China's wishful thinking, they will undoubtedly employ oppressive measures and gradually attempt to reclaim administrative rights over affiliated territories and the right to garrison troops after stationing them. It is not difficult to foresee them also imposing difficulties on us through political means. It is a sound principle to eliminate disputes before they escalate. It goes without saying that to uphold the empire's rightful position, we should adopt a firm attitude to counter this. Regarding the aforementioned first point, China's unreasonable freight rate competition, our nation (Japan) should take a resolute stance in response, making them realize the futility of competition. If we do not inflict a severe blow, engaging in discussions of compromise under the guise of "coexistence and co-prosperity" will be tantamount to surrender. The empire should not take such a path at this time. Regarding the second point above, the SMR encirclement plan, the Japanese Empire should vow to resist based on the prohibition of parallel and competing lines stipulated in the Beijing Agreement of 1905 (Meiji 38). Any railway plan that infringes upon these rights should be resolutely denied. To uphold the interests of that agreement, the empire should, if deemed necessary, adopt self-defense measures, expressing its intention to shatter China's delusions. Furthermore, the Jilin-Hunchun Railway and the Taonan-Angangxi-Jidun Railway, constructed with loans from us (Japan) despite the empire's protests, currently violate the original contracts. To uphold our nation's rights and interests, it is appropriate to adopt suitable measures. Furthermore, according to the Gando Convention, we should, at this time, compel China to allow our nation to construct the Jilin-Hui Railway. If they reject this request, our nation should explicitly declare the termination of the Gando Convention and restore the state of the border between our two countries along the Tumen River to its condition before the convention's establishment. Our demand to construct that railway is the price for relinquishing our claim to the territory of former Korea in the Gando region. If China does not sincerely deliver this price, the empire should deem China to have voluntarily relinquished the substance of the convention and proceed to occupy Gando as a matter of course.

Regarding the Concession Issue, the return of concessions is a long-standing plan of the Chinese government. Their current request for the return of our Hankou concession is merely a manifestation of this plan. Our government should refuse, stating that the return of concessions should not be discussed until the issue of extraterritoriality is resolved, adhering to this policy without any alteration. The Chinese side's success in reclaiming the British concessions in Jiujiang and Hankou the year before was nothing short of a forceful seizure. We must ensure that such incidents are not repeated. We should use our strength to protect our concessions. The empire's position and rights in the Shanghai International Settlement are equal to those of Britain. Given that the number of our residents is several times greater than that of the British, we should uphold our nation's position in the Shanghai International Settlement. Furthermore, regarding the future fate of that settlement, the empire should always hold a significant position and rights.

Regarding the Issue of Extraterritoriality, abolishing extraterritoriality in one fell swoop is practically impossible given China's current circumstances. Even Britain and the United States advocate for a gradual abolition. If we can coordinate with the empire on matters of mutual interest and jointly reject this unreasonable demand, ensuring that we do not engage in unsightly concessions or appeasement, that would be ideal. Furthermore, administrative rights over affiliated territories do not fall within the scope of trade but derive from the treaty by which our nation received these territories from Qing Russia in 1905 (Meiji 38). As we approach treaty revision, it is clear that there is no possibility of modifying that treaty.

Regarding the Issue of Foreign Loans, since the establishment of the Nanjing government, there have been frequent reports of comprehensive plans for loans from foreign loan syndicates, particularly the Manchurian-Mongolian railway network loans that oppress the SMR, which are suspect. Japan should alert the four-nation loan syndicate with whom we have agreements to the dangers of recklessly investing in China and consider whether to study specific measures for making substantial revisions to existing loan regulations, consulting with the great powers.

Regarding the Normalization of Sino-Japanese Relations, we should urge China to reflect on the slogans of abolishing unequal treaties and overthrowing imperialism and crack down on anti-Japanese content in Chinese textbooks and materials that incite animosity in Chinese youth. We should seriously negotiate with China to ensure their elimination, preventing harm to the peace between the two countries. Furthermore, to maintain the overall situation in East Asia and enhance friendly relations with neighboring countries, Japan should establish appropriate propaganda organs in various parts of China to facilitate propaganda and enlighten the Chinese populace about the harmony of Sino-Japanese relations. Currently, it is generally acknowledged that our nation's diplomacy towards China is weak. For the fundamental interests of the empire, we should adhere to the following conditions: (1) respect treaties and ensure diplomatic prestige; (2) secure our nation's rights and interests in Manchuria; and (3) uphold the interests of Koreans in Manchuria. Since the Washington Conference, our country has demonstrated a spirit of international cooperation and made significant concessions in its diplomacy towards China. However, not only have we received no recompense, but we have also encouraged their recklessness. The disregard for treaties in Manchuria is a prime example. Is it not lamentable that this has led to our country's isolation in the world? If we continue to employ stopgap measures without a fundamental guarantee policy, I fear that the relinquishment of our rights and interests in Manchuria and Mongolia will occur over time, and we will only gain a reputation for "co-prosperity." This association, in deliberating on emergency countermeasures against China, transcends all policies and political factions, aiming for consistent spirit. It is our earnest hope that the SMR will be brought to a competitive victory. To overcome these difficulties, we hope that the nation will rouse its spirit, that the government and the people will unite, and that all sectors will foster a great-nation mentality. Then, the reach of our authority will not only enhance our national prestige. We hope you will appreciate this. (June 6th)

The Opposition to Production and Sales Taxes by the Business Community in Hebei Remains Fierce 81

Businesses in All Sectors Halt the Shipment of Goods

A Final Decision to Continue the Strike

Chambers of Commerce in Various Cities and Counties Appeal to Zhang

Tianjin News: Regarding the production and sales taxes in Hebei Province, the Tianjin business community previously sent representatives to Ping (Beijing) to petition Zhang Xueliang for their abolition. However, due to Zhang's illness, Chief of Staff Ji Yi of the Deputy Commander's Headquarters received them. At that time, Ji responsibly stated to the petitioning representatives that the taxes would be levied more leniently. However, according to investigations, as of the afternoon of the 3rd, the Tianjin East Station Production and Sales Tax Bureau and the Sugar Production and Sales Tax Bureau had not yet received a formal order from the Financial Commissioner's Office. Furthermore, a notice was issued to all trade associations. Therefore, a meeting was convened to discuss measures to address the production and sales taxes. Chairman Yang Wancheng first reported that he had received a telephone call from Beijing from the petitioning representatives remaining in Ping, reporting that they had met with Ji Yi, who verbally promised that the production and sales taxes in Ping and Tianjin would be temporarily suspended. In reality, such a verbal promise is insufficient, and we should continue our efforts and not stop until the goal of abolishing the taxes is achieved. Next, tea merchant representative Geng Richu proposed that since we have received a telephone call from Beijing stating that the taxes will be temporarily suspended, what steps should various sectors take? It was unanimously decided that various sectors should persevere to the end and not resume shipments or transportation until a formal announcement abolishing the production and sales taxes is seen, in order to achieve final victory. Subsequently, representatives from various sectors spoke one after another with great fervor, generally agreeing that the production and sales taxes would lead to the merchants' demise. Therefore, no matter what sacrifices are necessary, they would not relent until the production and sales taxes are completely abolished. On the 4th, a meeting continued, at which the petitioning representatives who went to Ping, Chen Chuxiang and Li Kuotian, reported on the progress of their negotiations in Ping and elected Chen Chuxiang as chairman. According to Chen's report, the petitioners went to Ping entrusted by the various sectors, and the glimmer of hope they had obtained was that Jing Youyan indicated that the production and sales taxes could be temporarily suspended. However, after seeing Chief of Staff Ji Yi, they were told that Special Commissioner Jing had no authority to make such a decision regarding the tax, so a decision could only be made after the Deputy Commander recovered from his illness. Because the authorities' methods are ambiguous, we were ultimately unable to achieve our goal. Although Beijing is also temporarily suspending the taxes, there are still instances of extortion. Tianjin's situation is even more different from Beijing's. Most of the import and export of goods passes through here. If this is not thoroughly resolved, it is tantamount to placing the business community in a deadly situation. We should discuss measures to address this in order to achieve our wishes. After discussion, it was decided to send representatives to Ping again to work with the Beijing business community to strive for the immediate abolition of the production and sales taxes. If there is still no satisfactory result and the authorities respond with ambiguous measures, we should continue with the previous proposal to strike in order to resist, etc.

Eighty-eight organizations of chambers of commerce from various cities and counties in Hebei Province specially prepared a document to Zhang Xueliang requesting the cancellation of the production and sales taxes. The original text reads: "Submitting a document concerning the harsh and burdensome production and sales taxes, which harm businesses and the people. We earnestly request that you order a fundamental cancellation to alleviate the hardships of businesses and relieve the distress of the people. Since the years of continuous warfare, the losses of Hebei's merchants and people have been the heaviest. Fortunately, the central government, mindful of the people's suffering, resolutely abolished the likin tax, and the vitality was slightly restored, and the people were overjoyed. Unexpectedly, the customs tax was increased and implemented on June 1st. Then, the production and sales tax and the business tax were successively introduced, pressing in upon us. Abolishing one likin tax and replacing it with three taxes has already greatly deviated from the purpose of abolishing the likin tax. Moreover, what is not produced? What goods are not sold? The items listed encompass everything, including even the daily necessities of small-scale operations such as shoulder-pole carriers and vendors of rice, flour, oil, and firewood. None can escape the production, sales, and business taxes. Such heavy levies and indiscriminate exactions are not only a transformed likin tax but are also a hundredfold worse than the likin tax. How can we, the surviving remnants, endure this? We have long admired your kindness and compassion, your advocacy of peace, and your prioritizing of the people's livelihood. Therefore, the representatives have come from afar to prostrate themselves and plead for your decisive action to strictly order the cancellation of the production and sales taxes on goods that harm businesses and the people, in order to relieve the suffering of the 30 million merchants and people of Hebei. The situation is urgent, and we have presumptuously submitted this document. We humbly request your consideration and implementation, and we await your orders. Respectfully presented by Tian Zhuobin, Chairman of the Julu County Chamber of Commerce, Jia Huipu and Wang Enpu, representatives of the Tangshan County Chamber of Commerce, Liu Songting, Zong Hanbo, and Wei Jiuyan, representatives of the Tong County Chamber of Commerce, and a total of eighty-eight organizations (June 5th)."

The Defeated Gang匪 Fled to Fujian and Were Repeatedly Defeated 82

Lu Xinming's Troops Recaptured Ruijin County

Fuzhou Correspondence: After the two contingents of Red bandits led by Zhu De and Peng Dehuai from Guangchang and Ningdu in eastern Jiangxi were defeated by the Sixth Route Army led by Zhu Shaoliang and the Twenty-sixth Route Army led by Sun Lianzhong, they regrouped with 5,000 to 6,000 men in Lichuan and Nanfeng and fled into Guangze and Jianning counties in northern Fujian. They were severely suppressed by the troops stationed in Guangze, led by Lin Bingzhou, and the troops stationed in Jianning, led by Liu Shang. They then fled from Guangze and Jianning into Shaowu and TaiNing, plotting to use Shaowu as a base to connect with the two contingents of Fang Zhimin and Shao Shiping in Chong'an and Pucheng, vainly attempting to rise up again. The provincial government repeatedly received reports and telegraphed Liu Heding's division to encircle and suppress them, preventing them from creating disturbances. Liu's divisional troops have now concentrated in Shunchang and are advancing towards Shaowu. At the same time, Qian Yuguang and Lin Bingzhou's two brigades have concentrated in Chong'an and are advancing towards Guangze, attacking from both sides to put them in a situation of facing enemies on both their front and rear. A major battle is expected to occur between Shaowu and Guangze within a day or two. Another contingent of Red bandits invaded Fujian from Ruijin on the Jiangxi border, attempting to connect with the local Red bandits in western Fujian's military towns of Longyan, Shanghang, and Yongding. The First Detachment of the Western Fujian Bandit Suppression Forward Command, led by Lu Xinming, intercepted them head-on at Gucheng, a place on the border between Fujian and Jiangxi. The bandit forces were unable to withstand the attack and retreated back into Ruijin. Captain Lu then dispatched Regiment Commander Ma Hongxing to track and pursue them. The bandits collapsed upon seeing them. Regiment Commander Ma captured the county seat of Ruijin. The regiment is now coordinating with friendly forces to advance and thoroughly eliminate the remaining bandits. (June 6th)

The Circumstances of Hu Zuyu's Death from Injuries 83

Zhou Hunyuan Serves as Acting Commander of the Fifth Division

Nanchang Correspondence: Hu Zuyu, commander of the Fifth Division, was shot in the abdomen during a fierce battle with Red bandits in Guangchang on May 27. He was escorted to the provincial capital by the division headquarters and admitted to Nanchang Hospital on June 2 for treatment. Due to the severity of his injuries, he passed away at 5:50 PM on the 3rd. The encoffining ceremony was held at the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall at 10:00 PM on the 4th. The Fifth Division's troops are currently under the command of Deputy Division Commander Zhou Hunyuan. The detailed circumstances are recorded below:

Circumstances of the Injury: At 5:00 AM on May 27, tens of thousands of Red bandits attacked Guangchang. The troops stationed in the city were the Fifth Division and the Twenty-fourth Division, under the command of Zhu Shaoliang. Hu Zuyu, commander of the Fifth Division, at that time personally supervised the troops and bravely suppressed the bandits on the front line. The bandits repeatedly launched fierce assaults, but they were all repelled. The casualties among the Red bandits were numerous. The intensity of the battle was unprecedented since the bandit suppression efforts in Jiangxi Province began. Later, Hu planned to send troops to outflank the bandits from the left wing and cut off their retreat route. He climbed to the highest point to observe with binoculars. Unfortunately, at 7:30 AM, he was shot in the abdomen, the bullet entering below the right costal margin and exiting below the left posterior costal margin, also wounding his left arm. Despite being injured, he refused to retreat and continued to encourage the officers and soldiers to bravely advance, directing all strategies. He endured until he could no longer sustain himself and descended the mountain. After reaching the division headquarters, he collapsed on a bed, drenched in sweat, bleeding profusely, and vomiting a coffee-colored substance. He gradually fell into a coma. Zheng, the chief medical officer of the division, immediately administered cardiac stimulants, which stabilized him somewhat, and he gradually regained consciousness. He even made a phone call to report to Commander-in-Chief Zhu and frequently inquired about the battle situation.

Treatment Process: That afternoon at 5:00 PM, the division dispatched personnel to escort him away from Guangchang. On the 29th, he arrived in Nanfeng. At 3:00 AM on June 2, he arrived safely in Nanchang and was admitted to Ward 212 of Nanchang Hospital. Along the way, his pulse was 96 and his temperature was 38 degrees Celsius. After entering the hospital, doctors diagnosed that his stomach, liver, spleen, and other abdominal organs were injured, posing a risk of peritonitis. An enema was administered, and he was fed nutrient juice through the anus. According to the doctors, his stomach was injured, and there was concern that food would spill out of the wound, causing peritonitis, which was quite dangerous. In the afternoon of the 2nd, Minister He visited the hospital to express his condolences, and Hu inquired about the situation in Guangdong. Minister He then provided 3,000 yuan for medical expenses and instructed him to rest and recuperate. On the morning of the 3rd, Doctors Niu Huilin and Niu Huisheng from Shanghai arrived by plane to examine him. They stated that his lungs were also injured, posing a risk of pneumonia. Cardiac stimulants and sedatives were administered, and nutrient juice was infused. They said that the lower lobe of his left lung was severely inflamed due to the injury and that it would take a week to reach a safe condition. On that day, his pulse and temperature were normal, and Hu himself felt comfortable. However, at 5:00 PM that afternoon, he suddenly began to sweat profusely and vomit fresh blood. He passed away suddenly in just fifteen minutes, without leaving any last words to his family.

Moving the Coffin to the Park: Guo Su, chief of staff of the division, and Yao Chun, commander of the Fourteenth Brigade, were taking care of him in Nanchang. At 11:00 PM on the 3rd, they consulted with Provincial Department Directors Jiang and Gong and moved Hu's remains to the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall in Yuzhang Park. Zhang Muhan, director of the commander's office stationed in the province, was dispatched to report to Minister He. Minister He was extremely saddened by this tragic news and immediately instructed Director Zhang to handle Commander Hu's funeral generously. He also telegraphed the central government and Commander-in-Chief Jiang to offer generous compensation to console his heroic spirit.

The Encoffining Ceremony: Chairman Lu of the provincial government and all the committee members believed that Commander Hu had made outstanding contributions in suppressing bandits in Jiangxi and issued a special order yesterday for all provincial agencies, organizations, and schools to mourn in unison and send representatives to participate in the encoffining ceremony. The encoffining ceremony was held at 9:00 AM on the morning of the 4th. In addition to Minister He, who was unable to attend in person due to official duties and specially sent his aide-de-camp as his representative to pay respects, Chairman Lu and leaders from party, government, military, and business circles went to pay their respects and view the remains. Hu's family members were all in Suzhou. Only his elder brother Laisheng and younger brother Peizhi were present to view the encoffining. Hu was dressed in his lieutenant general's uniform with his command saber at his waist. The coffin was made of Phoebe zhennan wood and was worth 1,200 yuan. After the encoffining, the spirit tablet was placed in the center of the coffin, draped with a party flag and a national flag. Two wreaths were placed on either side of the spirit tablet, inscribed with the words "His Noble Spirit Lives On Forever." The Fifth Division headquarters telegraphed the entire division yesterday, ordering all officers and soldiers to wear black armbands. The provincial government's provincial affairs meeting yesterday was also suspended for one day in mourning. Furthermore, Chairman Lu instructed that Commander Hu's funeral should be handled solemnly and initiated the joint organization of funeral affairs by party, government, and military agencies. A funeral committee of nine people was appointed, nominated by various agencies.

The Anhui Provincial Government Rectifies the Business Tax 84

Ordering Various County Bureaus to Assist in Implementation

Anqing Correspondence: Since the implementation of the business tax in Anhui Province, there have been repeated setbacks due to the hesitant attitudes of merchants. Yesterday, the provincial government issued an urgent telegram ordering various county governments and public security bureaus to assist in the implementation and stipulating six regulations, strictly ordering all commissioners to comply. Excerpts from the two telegrams are recorded below: (1) Telegram to various county governments and public security bureaus: "The delay and obstruction in the implementation of the business tax in various counties is due to the hesitant attitudes of merchants, but it is also largely due to the control and covert manipulation by chambers of commerce. Although commissioners have reported that more than twenty districts have begun collecting the tax, the estimated capital and business income are mostly inaccurate, resulting in a significant loss of tax revenue. The delays and excuses for failing to report and pay the tax are even more unacceptable. The deadline for the first installment of taxes this year is approaching, and further delays or leniency are no longer possible. In addition to stipulating six regulations and strictly ordering all commissioners to comply, this telegram instructs the county and bureau chiefs to earnestly take responsibility and assist in the implementation. If any merchants refuse to be investigated or arbitrarily resist the tax, the county and bureau chiefs should jointly compel them to pay the tax and impose fines according to the regulations. If anyone in the chamber of commerce instigates resistance, their names should be ascertained and reported to this government for verification and action. As this matter concerns the provincial finances, this government will use it as a basis for evaluating the performance of the county and bureau chiefs. Do not show favoritism or cause inconvenience." (2) Telegram to various commissioners: "The business tax in various districts has been implemented for half a year. Although most commissioners have reported that they have begun collecting the tax, the estimated capital and business income of various industries are often filled out freely by the merchants without any actual investigation, which is mostly perfunctory. The delays and excuses for failing to collect the tax are even more unacceptable. The following regulations are hereby stipulated: (1) If the capital and business income filled out by various merchants are deemed inappropriate, they should be investigated according to the regulations, and their registers should be earnestly estimated. (2) The first installment of taxes for this year must be collected in full by the end of June. (3) All businesses with capital of more than 500 yuan are not allowed to request tax exemption, except as otherwise stipulated in the previously issued regulations. The commissioner shall not request tax exemption on this basis. (4) If any merchants refuse to be investigated or resist paying the tax, the commissioner shall send a letter to the county government to compel them to pay the tax and impose penalties according to the regulations. (5) If any chamber of commerce instigates resistance, the names of the instigators should be ascertained and reported to this government for verification and action. (6) If any commissioner continues to be dilatory or perfunctory, the Department of Finance will impose penalties accordingly. In addition to separate telegrams, this commissioner is ordered to strictly comply (June 7th)

The Shaanxi Relief Association Continues to Urge the Central Government to Issue Relief Funds 85

Various Counties Still Report Severe Disasters

Xi'an Correspondence: The Shaanxi Relief Association held its 28th committee meeting on May 27. The attending committee members were Kang Jiyao, Lu Hewen, Nan Hanchen, Wang Yishan, Wang Yinzhi, and Gao Jieren (representing Wang Yinzhi). The meeting was chaired by Kang Jiyao, who reported on incoming and outgoing documents. Next, representatives of disaster victims from Anbian, Dingbian, Chengcheng, and other counties reported on the disaster situation in their respective counties and requested the allocation of funds.

Page 9

Summary of Important News 86

A discussion on disaster relief led to the following resolutions: (1) Regarding the method of urging the central government to continue issuing relief funds, it was resolved to telegraph President Yu, the Shaanxi representatives in the National Assembly, and the relief association representatives to urge the central government to issue the funds. (2) Regarding how to dispose of the 100,000 yuan in relief funds that the central government has now issued, it was resolved to discuss it further after the funds arrive. (3) Regarding the severe shortage of draught cattle in the disaster areas, it was resolved to actively raise funds to purchase and transport them and to request that the provincial government strictly prohibit the slaughter of draught cattle, with severe penalties for those who slaughter and consume them. (4) Regarding how to regulate the agricultural implement pawn shops, which have been ordered to close, it was resolved to instruct the various pawn shops to notify farmers to redeem them without interest starting from June 1 to facilitate agricultural work. A temporary motion was made to establish rural cooperatives, and it was resolved to draft organizational methods or outlines separately. The meeting then adjourned.

The disaster situation in Shaanxi Province is still severe, and the cries of hunger from various counties continue unabated. The disaster situation reported by various counties is as follows: (1) In Chengcheng County, there has been no rain or snow since last winter. Since the beginning of spring, there has been no rain from the first to the fourth rain period. It was not until May that there was a light shower. The wheat crops that had been hoed were so sparse that those that did not wither and die were almost non-existent. The amount of rainfall in Chengcheng County is particularly scarce compared to the eastern and western areas, only one or two tenths. The wheat is immature, and cotton has not been planted. Not only is there no clothing or food to survive the year, but even the current livelihood is difficult to maintain. In recent months, cases of suicide have been reported in the eastern, western, southern, and northern areas of the county. Therefore, we hope for prompt relief. (2) The disasters and banditry in Ningxia County over the years are countless. The floods in 1926 and 1927 and the droughts in 1929 and 1930 have turned the original mulberry fields into the sea. The waters of the Meridian Avenue are difficult to traverse. The rich are impoverished in an instant, and the dead are buried in the bellies of fish. The suffering of the entire county from the flood is unprecedented in Ningxia. Unexpectedly, waves of bandits entered the territory last winter, the large bandit gangs of Peng Zhengang and others and countless unnamed small gangs arrived one after another. The cruelty of their trampling is indescribable. Suffering within suffering, pain within pain. Such disasters and banditry have been prolonged for six years. Exiles await rescue, and they will not survive without relief. (3) In the three northeastern districts of Weinan County, the damage was most severe from April 17 to May 2 or 3. A strong wind rose, and flying sand and rocks filled the sky, obscuring the sun. Tiled roofs shook, and trees were destroyed. The leaves of plants were completely covered by sand and rocks. Wheat, beans, and other crops were also damaged and withered. Even more so, the wheat seedlings were in the flowering stage and were destroyed by the wind, resulting in insufficient fruit set and small, weak grains. Therefore, the price of wheat has increased, and people's lives are difficult. Currently, people are digging up grass roots and peeling tree bark to eat to fill their stomachs.

Fuzhou Seizes Foreign-Branded Opium Dens 87

Taiwanese Who Opened Opium Dens Are Sent Back to Their Hometowns

However, the Taiwanese Still Secretly Sell Pure Opium Paste

Fuzhou Correspondence: Taiwanese people have been opening opium dens and earth platforms in Fuzhou and Xiamen, undermining our country's opium prohibition. Recently, the provincial government telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to lodge a serious protest with the Japanese minister. The Japanese minister then ordered the Japanese consul stationed in Fujian to have local opium prohibition agencies notify the consulate by telephone whenever Taiwanese open foreign-branded opium dens in Fujian. The consulate would then dispatch police to jointly investigate and confiscate the foreign-branded signs and repatriate the Taiwanese, emphasizing opium prohibition and upholding national honor. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed the provincial government to inform them of the matter and instructed them to handle it accordingly. After receiving the telegram, the provincial government immediately ordered the Opium Prohibition Committee to dispatch Commissioner Zhu Fuliang to the Japanese consulate to meet with Consul Tamura and request that the foreign-branded signs previously confiscated in joint operations by Chinese and Japanese police be sealed first. As for the repatriation of the Taiwanese, Consul initially evaded the issue, but after Commissioner Zhu's stern questioning, he finally agreed to comply. On May 27, he dispatched many Japanese and Taiwanese police officers from this office to various places, including Xiangxia Temple, Fanchuanpu, Fuxin Street, Zhoubian Street, Tudi Temple, Hechun Cheng, Nanmen Dou, Xiying Li, Xueyuan Qian, Macau Bridge, and Gaojie Li, to seal all 50-odd foreign-branded opium dens and earth platforms, including Yonglong, Gonghe, Yongtai, and Shiquan, which had been raided four to over ten times. The more than 100 Taiwanese who opened these shops were immediately repatriated. After this incident, the foreign firms that had not been sealed were greatly alarmed. Those with strong capital stopped operating to avoid losses, while those with smaller scale changed their tactics, stopped turning on the lights, and specialized in selling pure opium paste, shifting their business hours to after 5:00 PM (because the consulate has stopped working at this time) in an attempt to avoid the crackdown. The Opium Prohibition Committee is currently dispatching personnel to secretly investigate the brand names, locations, owners' names, and business hours in order to notify the Japanese consul and jointly crack down on them and pacify the opium atmosphere.

Zhenjiang Quick Dispatch 88

Due to the incomplete preparation of various registers for the demarcation of Jiangsu provincial and municipal boundaries, the reception period has been extended again. The Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday telegraphed the Nanjing Municipal Government, requesting it to expedite the appointment of personnel to jointly measure the boundaries. The Nanjing Municipal Government replied, stating that the boundaries had already been clearly demarcated and there was no need for further joint measurement.

The case of Chen Fu, Director of the Public Security Bureau of the provincial capital, being reported for alleged misconduct was addressed by the Control Yuan, which secretly telegraphed the Provincial Government, requesting a thorough investigation for submission to the National Government for handling. Upon receiving the telegram, the Provincial Government forwarded the original telegram to the Department of Civil Affairs, and the reported content involves two charges: corruption and dereliction of duty.

Zhong E, Director of the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Transportation, was ordered to inspect telecommunications in various counties north and south of the Yangtze River. He arrived in the province the day before yesterday and returned to Nanjing yesterday to report on his mission.

Jia Lin, Superintendent of the Jiang Customs, received an order from the Ministry of Finance yesterday to complete the closure of the Chang Customs within fifty *li* by the end of this month. Funds for indemnity payments will be allocated from export taxes. Expenditures incurred during the closure period are approved at one percent. All files and documents are to be transported to the Ministry for safekeeping.

Hangzhou Quick Dispatch 89

Governor Zhang of the Provincial Government proposed abolishing the Municipal Government to reduce expenditures. The proposal was approved by the Political Committee. However, considering the large scope of municipal affairs, it was decided not to halt operations immediately after abolishing the Municipal Government. Instead, a Municipal Affairs Committee will be established to manage municipal affairs.

The Provincial Government revised the Zhejiang Province Management Regulations for Mining and Transporting Yellow Sand.

The determined management fees and sand prices are appropriately reduced: 1. For sand mining land that is privately owned and either claimed or leased, a management fee of two *jiao* per ton of sand is to be paid, whether from offshore or inland rivers. 2. For sand mining land that is government-owned, a management fee of two *jiao* per ton of sand and a sand price of one *jiao* are to be paid, whether from offshore or inland rivers. Jiang, Director of the Zhejiang Province Mineral Resources Survey Institute, plans to go to Qu County and Changshan area soon to explore coalfield regions.

The Department of Construction stated that farmers' banks or loan offices have not been established in various counties formerly under the Wenzhou and Chuzhou prefectures, hindering farmers' production prospects. To alleviate the rural economy, a special order was sent to the Provincial People's Bank to establish offices in Wenzhou and Chuzhou prefectures to assist agriculture.

The Zhejiang Provincial Business Tax is currently scheduled by the Department of Finance to begin collection on the 11th of this month. However, various businesses in Hangzhou City believe that the business tax rate is unfair compared to Shanghai and Hangzhou, and they still intend to present their case to the Provincial Finance Department, requesting a reduction. Local Correspondence

Songjiang 90

A robbery occurred at Xianghua Bridge. An elderly woman named Nie, residing in Changqiao South, returned home disappointed. While walking across Xianghua Bridge, a young man, about twenty years old, dressed in a Western suit, ran up and told her that Mr. Zhang had returned, asking her to go back. As the woman turned around to go back, the young man snatched the gold hairpin from her hair and fled. At that time, the location was quiet and secluded, with no pedestrians on the road. The elderly woman shouted "Robbery!" and only then did pedestrians passing by hear the sound and begin to chase after the thief, but he had already disappeared. Subsequently, a patrol officer from the Second Precinct passed by and, according to the woman's report, immediately reported the incident by phone to the patrol supervisor, who dispatched police to various jewelry stores to inquire and sent plainclothes police to lie in wait for the thief. Unexpectedly, at Zerun Bridge, the Shicheng Silver Shop claimed that a young man in a Western suit had come to exchange a gold hairpin. He seemed unhappy with the value of one yuan and two and a half *jiao* and still kept it. The police chased westward but failed to catch him. However, when the woman reported to the patrol officer, she said that the gold hairpin weighed five *qian*, which was likely a false statement. The young man also seemed to realize that it was not real gold and was greatly disappointed.

Suzhou 91

British Consulate in Shanghai Inquires About the Case of a Killed Military Police Officer. A military police officer of the road protection squad, 1st Company, 1st Battalion, 1st Regiment of the Military Police stationed in Suzhou, was shot and killed by someone on the railway in Zhengyi, Kunshan, several days ago, and two others were wounded by gunfire. Subsequently, a foreigner was captured by soldiers there and escorted to the Military Police Regiment headquarters in Suzhou, awaiting disposition. Yesterday (the 9th), the British Vice-Consul in Shanghai, Sakato, inquired at the county government about whether the foreigner captured was the British man, William Talbot (19 years old), who had gone missing from Shanghai at the time of the incident. County Magistrate Huang immediately stated that he had received a telegram from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs ordering an investigation to determine whether the person was Russian or British. He had sent a letter to the Military Police Regiment but had not yet received a reply. Once he received a reply, he would immediately inform the Consul. Sakato then left and returned to Shanghai that evening.

The Dispute over Encroachment on Ancient Sites Remains Unresolved. The New Suzhou Farm planned to encroach on the remaining land of the Yishan Tantai Academy outside Fengmen Gate, where Yin Hejing studied, to build a farm. After several negotiations, the provincial government ordered that the ancient site of Yin Hejing's study place be demarcated and preserved, and the farm was allowed to claim the remaining land. Yesterday, County Magistrate Huang received an order from Governor Ye of the provincial government, stating that the New Suzhou Farm in the county had reported claiming a total of 18 *mu*, 5 *li*, and 2 *hao* of mountain land in Yishan, of which 6 *mu*, 9 *fen*, 6 *li*, and 6 *hao* were mountain land with four stone pillars and a stone tablet, which can be recorded as the site of Tantai Academy. It should be preserved. If only 2 *li* are demarcated for the preservation of ancient sites, it seems to be inconsistent with the original plan. He should be ordered to consult on a solution and submit it for review. The Shi family's gravesite was said to be demarcated by the New Suzhou Farm, together with the Shi family descendants and the gravesite preservation association, who independently divided the boundary markers. He should be ordered to draw a map of the agreed boundary and submit it for record. As for Mr. Yin Hejing's study place, the New Suzhou Farm also submitted that the records claimed that it was indeed in Tiger Hill, and the county should conduct a detailed investigation and reply for verification. He should be ordered to comply with the handling and first inform the New Suzhou Farm. The steles, records, photos, and drawings are all on file.

Wu County Establishes a Bandit Suppression Command Headquarters for Taihu Lake. The governors of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, due to the instability caused by bandits in Taihu Lake, decided to thoroughly eliminate them. They specially appointed Zhu Mian, commander of the First Security Regiment of Jiangsu and commander of the Suzhou-Changzhou Pacification Area, as the temporary commander for coordinating the suppression of long-standing bandits in Taihu Lake, and Wang Zhiqi, commander of the Second Security Regiment of Zhejiang, as the deputy commander. They were ordered to immediately prepare for the suppression. After being appointed, Commander Zhu immediately established a command headquarters in Suzhou to facilitate coordination and sent adjutant Wang Jiayou and Zhang Qiao to Suzhou to jointly survey the address with County Magistrate Huang near Xumen. He then dispatched four infantry companies to Suzhou to station at various key points and suppress bandits as the opportunity arose. All expenses of the unit will be allocated 5,000 yuan by the province through Wu County for application.

Wuxi 92

Chamber of Commerce Telegrams to Request the Removal of Liyang County Magistrate. Liyang County Magistrate Li Jinfang, on the 30th of last month, suddenly used extraordinary means to surround the county's Chamber of Commerce with armed police. At the same time, four standing committee members of the chamber, including Shi Junsheng, Di Dechen, Hu Guoguang, and Sun Zuze, were detained and forced to confess late at night. Afterward, the chamber sent telegrams to various parties to appeal. As a result, the local county's Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Zhenjiang Provincial Government's Department of Civil Affairs for assistance and requested that Li Jinfang be removed from office and investigated to ensure compliance with the law. It is now heard that the chambers of commerce in Jiangsu Province are all outraged by this case and have already addressed Fang and Zhang, requesting that the county magistrate be severely punished.

Food Shops Disregard Hygiene; Police Bureau Punishes by Detention. Xu Jigui, director of the local Public Security Bureau, recently, with the arrival of summer, found that most food shops in the city did not cover their food with gauze, which was truly disregarding hygiene. He specially ordered health instructors to investigate the food shops. As a result of finding that some shops did not use gauze covers, the owners were detained and held by the bureau. There were over fifty cases. While each food shop recognized that the bureau was following proper procedures, they also said there had been no prior notice, and the detentions and punishments were too harsh. Therefore, they reported to the restaurant, meat, and other three trade associations, requesting assistance. The associations, upon receiving the reports, separately convened emergency meetings to discuss the results. They felt that this matter greatly hindered commercial order. Yesterday, the leaders of the associations, Ren Shuyin, Gu Ziyi, Wang Juting, and others, led over fifty members to the County Public Security Bureau to petition. Director Xu came out to meet the representatives, who stated their opinions in the petition. Director Xu stated that the bureau had repeatedly emphasized hygiene matters, but the shops had ignored them. Therefore, the bureau had to use decisive means to punish those who violated the rules. The intention was to punish one as a warning to a hundred. Since everyone had come to inquire today, the bureau would be lenient. The representatives felt that the results were quite satisfactory, so they bid farewell and left.

Changzhou 93

Silk Cocoon Store at Beigang Bridge Burns Down. In the western part of Wuyi County, only the Xinhua Silk Cocoon Store at Beigang Bridge was open this year, so the purchase of goods was quite strong. The store stopped purchasing goods on the 7th, having collected more than 300 *dan*. Unexpectedly, around 4 a.m. on the 8th, a fire suddenly broke out, spreading to the entire building. Although urgent efforts were made to put out the fire, it had already spread and the entire building and the collected cocoons were destroyed, with losses totaling approximately 20,000 yuan. Fortunately, there was fire insurance, so there is hope for compensation. A Torn Ransom Note Body Was Found at Chou City Bridge. Jiang Yinsheng, a bandit who was executed by firing squad in Jiangyin last year in August or September, kidnapped Xue Zhuchu, a resident of Xiqiao in the 5th district of the city, and demanded a ransom. Unable to obtain the ransom, Jiang tore up the ransom note and abandoned Xue's body. Xue's son was also killed by Jiang's gang and used as pig and dog feed. The means were cruel and shocking. After Jiang's execution, Xue's wife, remembering her husband's death a year prior and his bones still unburied, searched everywhere. Eventually, she went to Chou City Bridge in Wuyi and, on the 6th of this month, under the guidance of Hou Minggen (Jiang had paid Hou two silver dollars to help bury the body), discovered a body by the riverbank with its knees exposed. The body had not decayed, and the face was as it was in life, but the top of the head was covered in blood and the whole body was covered in dirt. Xue's wife recognized it as her husband's body. She immediately prepared a coffin, collected the body, and transported it back for burial. As for Hou Minggen, he was suspected of being an accomplice of the bandit and was summoned to the 4th District Office yesterday for questioning and supervision pending investigation.

Fengxian 94

The Sanxing Robbery Case in Shaji is Cracked. Chen Xuezhu, Director of the Third Public Security Bureau, previously received a tip that Wu Guisheng, Zhou A'gen, and other bandits who robbed Zhang Shengtang and Yan Guichun in Sanxing township were hiding near Datuan, on the border of Fengnan, inside a certain family's ancestral tomb. He immediately led police detectives to the area at night, captured the two bandits, and escorted them to the county.

Page 10

They confessed to the crimes during interrogation. However, Wu Guisheng confessed that he was already sixty-four years old and no longer had the strength to commit robbery. He only learned about the Zhang and Yan cases after the fact from someone who came to tell him, and he did not know if the pongee and other items given to him were stolen goods. In addition to ordering the summoning of the victims to identify and verify, the investigating officer Zhou ordered the police to apprehend all the fugitives involved in the case, both land and water police, yesterday.

Zhenjiang 95

Water Police Team to be Reorganized. Due to the rampant banditry in Taihu Lake, which is difficult to eliminate, the Jiangsu Provincial Government plans to abolish all district offices of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police and reorganize them into a Water Police Bureau specifically responsible for suppressing bandits in Taihu Lake. Therefore, the heads of the First, Second, Third, Fifth, and Sixth districts were summoned to the province the day before yesterday to discuss reorganization measures. The plan is divided into two parts: the inner lake and the outer sea. The inner lake will be responsible for suppressing bandits in Taihu Lake, and the outer sea will be responsible for suppressing bandits in the Yangtze River and the sea. The plan is said to have been finalized and is scheduled to be implemented on July 1.

In addition to convening a meeting of churches in Yangzhou from the 21st to the 28th to hold a prayer meeting in the hope of preventing disaster and saving the Chinese nation, they also telegraphed the National Christian Council of China in Shanghai to ask for their endorsement and notify churches across the country to hold a unified public prayer as scheduled. It is said that Zhang Zhijiang plans to fast in his room for a day for the country on the 7th.

A Guard Commits Shady Deal in an Opium Case and is Detained. Ling Shusheng, a guard in the Dongguan defending city, recently discovered several bags of opium in a traveler's handbag while on duty. Liyang 97

The Intricate and Complex Liyang Corruption Case. Liyang County Magistrate Li Jinfang reported the second corruption case in Liyang County, alleging that the former Director of the Finance Bureau, Pan Keping, who has now been transferred to the Finance Bureau of Jiangning County, conspired with Shi Junsheng and others from the Standing Committee of the Liyang County Chamber of Commerce to embezzle public funds. Initially, Li arrested the four Standing Committee members of the Chamber of Commerce, but the Department of Civil Affairs reprimanded him for acting hastily. Li felt that he was being punished for official duties and telegraphed the province to resign. Upon hearing the news, the parks in the county telegraphed the province to request that he be retained. Pan Keping, who was reported, also telegraphed the provincial government yesterday to defend himself, saying that Li's accusations were completely false. The Supervisory Committee of the Liyang County Chamber of Commerce also sent an express telegram, stating that they were illegally detained and forced to confess by Li's abuse of power. The case is intricate and complex, and both the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance have sent personnel to investigate. The various news are described as follows:

Li Jinfang's Resignation Letter: To Ye, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and Hu Jun, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs: The county's Finance Bureau discovered a second major corruption case. I secretly telegraphed the Department of Civil Affairs, requesting the Jiangning County Magistrate to detain Director Pan Keping first to prevent him from escaping and requesting permission to send the case file to the province for review. It has been six days without instructions. In this case, the Standing Committee of the Chamber of Commerce conspired to embezzle and solicit bribes, and the evidence is solid. A formal investigation is a proper procedure. Afterward, I only supervised them, did not abuse power, and did not detain them. However, Peng Jin, a Standing Committee member of the Chamber of Commerce, fled out of fear of punishment and fabricated accusations. The Director reprimanded me in a telegram on the day before yesterday, saying that County Magistrate Li of Liyang was accused by Peng Jin, a Standing Committee member of the Chamber of Commerce, of abuse of power and requested assistance. The County Magistrate acted hastily and should be reprimanded. The members of the Chamber of Commerce, including Shi Junsheng, Di Dechen, Hu Guoguang, and Sun Zuze, should be released first, pending investigation. Hu Zhiyin, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, and others, obeyed the order. I was punished for official duties, and I have no complaints. However, I feel that I have failed to fulfill my duties and have caused the superiors to worry. It is useless to stay here, so I am resigning. In addition to sending the entire file of Pan Keping and the Standing Committee of the Chamber of Commerce jointly committing corruption for review to the court for investigation, I respectfully request that personnel be sent to replace me as soon as possible. I await your orders. Li Jinfang, Acting County Magistrate of Liyang, respectfully submitted.

Pan Keping's Defense Telegram: To Ye, Chairman of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government, and Hu, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, and Chen, Director of the Department of Finance: I was shocked to read the oil-printed document of Liyang County Magistrate Li Jinfang's accusation of a second financial corruption in Liyang County. All new and old payments made by me during my tenure in Liyang Finance were made in accordance with legal procedures, and I have not made any mistakes. The allegations made by County Magistrate Li are completely false. In addition to submitting the details in a separate document, I respectfully request your review and verification. Pan Keping respectfully submitted.

Yesterday, the Supervisory Committee of the Liyang Chamber of Commerce also issued an express telegram to various newspapers and chambers of commerce, requesting justice, stating that Li had disagreements with Pan and wanted to make things difficult for him, inciting the Chamber of Commerce to fabricate false evidence. Initially, he used sweet words to deceive, then he used violence and coercion, and finally, he sent police to surround the Chamber of Commerce, search files and books, and arrest four Standing Committee members, detaining them in the police team headquarters and opening court late at night, forcing them to confess. They have now telegraphed the provincial government for a thorough investigation and punishment. Since the incident, the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance have sent personnel to conduct a secret investigation. The Department of Finance also sent inspector Ye Yongqing to investigate.

After investigating the accounts of the former Director of the Finance Bureau of Liyang, Pan Keping, the embezzlement of public funds was reported by the provincial government. County Magistrate Li was ordered to conduct a thorough investigation and, at the request of the local government, ordered Director Zhu to supervise the handover. It was later found that the Chamber of Commerce borrowed 35,000 yuan for purchasing guns, with a confirmed rebate of 5,000 yuan. County Magistrate Li felt that it was a matter of corruption and summoned the Standing Committee members of the Chamber of Commerce to inquire about the details. The members, fearing that they had committed bribery, hesitated and said that the accounts were handled by Peng Jin. County Magistrate Li only supervised them at the Dahua Hotel while awaiting Peng Jin's arrival and did not detain or imprison them. Unexpectedly, Peng, fearing punishment, fled to the province and fabricated facts, falsely accusing the government. In fact, the shops were very happy about this matter. Once the provincial government investigates and clarifies the matter, the truth will come out.

Jiangyin 98

The Soldier of the Arsenal Commits Assault. Ji Yongji, a soldier in the Qinwang Mountain Arsenal, accidentally collided with Dai Yu Zhang's son, Deqi, in Yuecheng Town, 11th district, a few days ago. Without asking the reason, Ji immediately beat Deqi severely. Deqi was young and timid and fled home. His father, Yu Zhang, questioned him and Ji chased him to the doorstep and beat Yu Zhang. Ji was not satisfied, ran to the street, grabbed a kitchen knife from the Longyuan Restaurant, and ran around the street, intending to kill people. Pedestrians avoided him. The A-Group there did their best to persuade him, but Ji was still as crazy as a lunatic. The district chief Li, upon hearing the report, immediately sent a group of soldiers from Qingyi to suppress him, but Ji had already escaped. The merchants and residents, because Ji was so violent, specially sent a letter to district chief Li, requesting Commander Yang of the fortress to investigate and punish Ji Yongji to reassure the merchants and residents.

The Bandit Xu Zhenru is Arrested. Xu Zhenru of Shuidang Village, 5th Section, Yunting, previously helped Wu Zhengrong, the police chief in Wuxi. However, due to some incident, he was dismissed and became a bandit. He committed crimes in Suzhou and Wuxi. Gong Guanying is Safe. Gong Guanying of Zhouzhuang was kidnapped in Jingmen. Zeng Zhiben reported yesterday that Gong telegraphed from Jingmen, Hubei Province, reporting to Zheng Cunchong Middle School that his brother Gong Jiguang was safe. The news was immediately reported to his family.

Pan A'qiao Commits Suicide Due to a Quarrel. Zhan Xiangzhou, commander of the Fortress, who lived in Junshan Alley, North Gate, married a woman surnamed Pan, A'qiao, last year. Plot to Kidnap a Western Doctor; Suspects Transferred to Court. A Corrupt Patrol Officer is Sent to Court for Interrogation. Pinghu 100

Zhouxu Town Suffers Second Looting. Zhoujiaxu Town, outside the East Gate of Pinghu, after being looted by bandits last autumn, those with some assets fled. Recently, the bandit leader was arrested, and the people's hearts were stabilized. Unexpectedly, at around 6 p.m. on the 7th, more than a dozen bandits armed with guns rushed to the town and looted many shops, including Wang Tongmao Meat Shop, Ma Yumao Fish Shop, Ding Hewan General Merchandise Store, and Shunxing Wine Shop. Because the town's defense forces and self-defense corps did not offer any resistance, they allowed them to loot for two hours before leaving with their spoils. It is estimated that the losses amounted to about a thousand gold pieces.

A Patrol Team Policeman Commits Adultery and Abducts a Rural Woman. Zhou Jun, a policeman in the county government's patrol team, seduced and abducted Lin Chengbao, the daughter-in-law of Peng Lin of Qingxiqiao, to escape to the city. Yesterday, Peng Lin learned the truth and came to the city to inquire. He met his daughter-in-law on East Main Street and persuaded her to go home. Chengbao, infatuated with lust, refused to return. Peng Lin twisted her to the Public Security Bureau and told the patrol team leader Zhou Pengfei the details. Team Leader Zhou was furious and immediately dismissed policeman Zhou and sent him to the county for legal action. Lin Chengbao was taken home by her mother-in-law.

A Counterfeit Money Offender is Apprehended. Yesterday, a man named Yin Yunchu used a five-yuan counterfeit banknote from Jiaotong Bank at He Zhengda's General Merchandise Store in Xudai East Market to purchase goods. The store was unaware and accepted the banknote. Later, the offender went to Hong Shunli Store in West Market and again used a counterfeit banknote. The store noticed the banknote and questioned Yin's origin. Yin stammered and fled east. He was spotted by He Zhengda, who intercepted and captured him and sent him to the Zhapu Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Hangzhou 101

A Robbery Occurs at Baziqiao. Baziqiao of Wukang Building is adjacent to Shangqianbu of Hang County. The other evening, four bandits armed with pistols suddenly arrived and robbed over a hundred silver yuan from tea drinkers in a tea shop. An unsuspecting guest who happened to be passing by was also robbed of fourteen yuan. They then robbed a family surnamed so-and-so of over one hundred yuan, for a total loss of over three hundred yuan. It has been reported to the Water and Land Police Bureau for investigation and arrest.

Killing With a Knife Over Debt Collection. Zhang Akun, a resident of the Hushu Tiaolu district, is a farmer. His wife is known to be violent. Because Wang Naibing, a resident of Zhongba, owed Zhang forty-nine yuan and five *jiao* for mulberry leaves, he requested an extension for repayment, but it was not granted. Around 4 p.m. yesterday, Zhang went to Wang's place again to demand payment, creating a menacing atmosphere. The two sides went from quarreling to fighting. At that time, Zhang stabbed Wang's left leg with a kitchen knife, causing a serious wound and heavy bleeding. Wang immediately fell to the ground unconscious. Zhang, seeing that he had caused trouble, took the opportunity to escape without a trace. Wang's family is currently in serious negotiations with the Zhang family.

A Small Loss of Four *Jiao* Costs a Life. Because his friend Jin A'lai owed him four *jiao*, Xu Shunsheng of Pingyao went to collect the debt yesterday. Jin ignored him, causing a quarrel. Jin suddenly reported it to the Public Security Bureau, which immediately sent police to investigate. Xu, who was washing his feet at Sunjia Bridge, suspected that he was going to be arrested, became flustered and cold, and accidentally fell into the water and drowned. The police station in charge of the area reported it to the Hangzhou District Court. Prosecutor Tong, along with police officers, went to examine the body. It was determined that he had fallen into the water and drowned. The death certificate was filled out, and the body was coffined and prepared for burial.

Xiaoshan 102

Robbery in Tangshan Bay Wounds a Person. Gao Heqin, a farmer in Tangshan Bay in eastern Xiaoshan, was able to make a living through hard work. Recently, he sold silkworm cocoons and had some cash, which was coveted by bandits. On the night of the 5th, five or six bandits wielding wooden clubs broke into his house. They first confined Gao's wife and daughters to one room, then went upstairs and looted clothing and cash worth over 500 yuan. At that time, a worker named Ah Huan was shot in the leg. After an hour, they fled with their spoils to the Waisha area.

A Rice Association Employee is Detained for Embezzlement. A Fan, an employee of the Rice Industry Council in Xiaoshan City, was planning to escape after embezzling public funds of the Council. The Council learned of the matter and reported it to the Public Security Bureau, which dispatched police to arrest Fan and escort him to the Public Security Bureau. In addition to confiscating the original embezzlement of over 70 yuan, he was also dismissed from his position as accounting clerk.

A Madman and a Madwoman Drown Together. On the afternoon of the 7th, a rural woman with a Shaoxing accent, who appeared to be insane, committed suicide by jumping into the river at Xixing Riverbank. Passersby spotted her and pulled her up, but she was already dead. On the same afternoon, at around 4 p.m., a man in his thirties from Xixing, who also appeared to be insane, was washing his feet and swimming in a mud pit near the Longtu Temple and suddenly drowned. The man and woman both died in the water, truly as the saying goes, "Nothing is alone."

Important News 103

The Ministry of Education Commends Donors Who Fund Education

Zheng Hongnian Discusses the Difficulty of Practice Versus Knowledge with Young People 110

Guanghua University held its weekly memorial service in the morning, and President Zheng Hongnian delivered a speech. The ceremony was conducted as usual. Chairman Zhang Shouyong reported on university affairs and gave a speech introducing and highly praising Zheng's enthusiasm for education, saying that the subsidies for private universities were thanks to Zheng's planning of the additional tax on deed verification when he was in the Ministry of Finance. Mr. Zheng's son is also studying at this university, which shows his close relationship with the university. In the future, he is planning to invite him to be a school director to help Guanghua develop.

Zheng then elaborated on the theory of the difficulty of practice versus knowledge, saying that the Book of Documents says that "to know is not difficult, to practice is difficult." At that time, he was already worried about the creed because there were customs and ethics in the Three Dynasties. Ethics are nothing more than filial piety and brotherly respect. It seems easy to be filial to parents and respectful to elder brothers, but it is not possible to actually do it. Therefore, there is the saying that "to know is not difficult, to practice is difficult." Scholars in the Tang, Han, Song, and Yuan dynasties generally did not change this. It was not until Wang Yangming of the Ming dynasty advocated the unity of knowledge and action. Commentators said that Japan's strength was deeply rooted in Yangming's ideas. Dr. Sun Yat-sen completely proved the difficulty of practice and the ease of knowledge from a scientific perspective. In terms of time, it is moving forward. Modern young people have a great desire for knowledge, which is very good. In the future, the responsibility of society lies with the youth. Leaders are also to be made by the youth. Is it good or bad to have the idea of being a leader? Just ask whether it conforms to logic or not. There is a difference of a thousand miles. Young people should strive for true knowledge and true understanding. If they can have inventions and creations in academics and gain social belief, then they will be leaders without being asked to be leaders. Therefore, first seek true knowledge and then strive to practice, which is the way for young people to become leaders.
