China National Amateur Athletic Federation

Amateur Sports Rules Established 115

The China National Amateur Athletic Federation, in conjunction with this year's National Games, has established the China National Amateur Athletic Federation's amateur sports rules as follows:

Aim of Amateur Sports 116

The China National Amateur Athletic Federation has established the following aims for determining the amateur qualifications of Chinese athletes participating in various sports competitions, such as international, national, regional, provincial, and county:

(1) Professional athletes in a certain sport, or those who knowingly become professional athletes, may not participate in that sport or any other sport.

(2) Amateur athletes may not receive monetary compensation or rewards for participating in sports competitions that would compensate them for the loss of their salaries.

Definition of Amateur Sports 117

Article 1: Amateur athletes participate in competitions solely for the love of sports.

Article 2: An athlete who participates in any sports competition for money or other benefits, or who obtains extra benefits on top of the due expenses for clothing and accommodation, becomes a professional athlete in any sport.

Article 3: An athlete who knowingly participates in the same team or competition against professional athletes without the permission of the responsible senior authority becomes a professional athlete.

Article 4: Anyone who teaches, trains, or guides athletes or engages in any physical education work and receives a salary is a professional athlete.

Article 5: Anyone who knowingly becomes a professional athlete can never regain their amateur status.

Article 6: Amateur athletes may not gamble or be involved in gambling on the sports competitions they participate in.

Article 7: Amateur athletes may not participate in any sports competition that awards prizes or souvenirs without any suitable inscriptions.

Article 8: The value of prizes won by amateur athletes may not exceed 100 local currency coins, unless specially permitted by the China National Amateur Athletic Federation.

Article 9: Amateur athletes may not sell, mortgage, or donate their prizes. These prizes must be kept for inspection by the China National Amateur Athletic Federation at any time.

Article 10: Amateur athletes may not impersonate or use other people's names to join any competition.

Article 11: When attending a meeting, participating in a competition, or returning from a sports meeting, amateur athletes may not receive any money or other benefits other than the actual expenses for train, boat, and accommodation. In any case, the expenses may not exceed the ordinary price of a passenger seat on the train or boat and 10 yuan per day or its equivalent for accommodation. If the meeting provides accommodation, the daily allowance per person may not exceed two local currency coins.

Article 12: Amateur athletes may not accept travel expenses or any expenses for their trainers, masseurs, or relatives.

(Note:) (The meaning of this article is not that the travel expenses of trainers, etc., cannot be paid, but that this expense cannot be requested by the athlete or paid to the athlete.)

Article 13: Amateur athletes may not receive direct or indirect compensation for joining a sports association or other sports organization as a member or continuing their membership.

Article 14: Amateur athletes should issue receipts separately for any money received. These receipts should be properly kept for inspection by the China National Amateur Athletic Federation at any time.

Article 15: Athletes who sell sports equipment are not considered professional athletes.

Article 16: Amateur athletes may not receive compensation for using the products of a certain company, factory, or retailer, nor may they use their names for advertising or promote the products of a certain company or factory for compensation.

Article 17: Amateur athletes may not use their own photos for store advertisements.

Article 18: An athlete who becomes a professional athlete without knowingly doing so can regain their amateur status after being suspended from competition for one year.

Article 20: An athlete who makes false reports about their qualifications, abilities, and achievements will lose their amateur status.

Article 21: Amateur competitions may not be promoted for personal gain.

Article 22: Amateur athletes may not serve as newspaper reporters and receive money for it at any sports competition (or part of a competition) in which they participate.

Article 23: When competing abroad, amateur athletes may receive money with the special permission of the China National Amateur Athletic Federation to purchase clothing or other personal items.

Recently Returned Tu Kaiyuan Excels in German Soccer 118

|German Sports Are Universally Developed|Many Talented Tennis Players Among Students Studying in Germany

In recent years, sports in China have gradually developed, and talents in various fields have emerged day by day. Overseas Chinese, influenced by what they see and hear, have also produced many special heroes, such as Qiu Feihai and Lin Baohua, tennis players who are famous in China today. There have also been many cases of students studying abroad who have special sports talents and who have taken over in foreign sports circles, reversing the guest-host relationship and occupying important positions. The achievements of Mr. Tu Kaiyuan, described below, are one such example.

Successful in Studying Medicine in Germany 119

Mr. Tu Kaiyuan went to Germany in 1923 and entered the University of Berlin to major in medicine. He graduated in 1928 with outstanding results. He was then sent by the university to various famous specialized hospitals for three years of internship before returning to China on May 1 of this year. He has temporarily set up a clinic in the Jicheng Pharmacy on Nanjing Road. Mr. Tu lived in Germany for ten years. In addition to studying medicine, he often devoted himself to the sports world to show his天赋 talent. In a few years, his reputation rose greatly, and everyone in Berlin knew his name.

Mr. Tu Kaiyuan 120

He is especially well-known in the soccer world. He also likes tennis, but he is not as good at it as he is at soccer. The reporter knew him ten years ago. Now, we meet again in our hometown. We had a long night of pleasant conversation, especially about sports matters. The following is a record of our conversation, which reads as if you are in the middle of it. It is full of interest and details the latest trends in German sports and the activities of students studying in Germany in the sports world. It is full of interest, as if you are on the scene. The following is a written account to introduce the great achievements of our students in the German sports world and to clarify one aspect of recent German sports.

Constant Struggle Leads to Fame 121

When Mr. Tu arrived in Berlin, Germany in 1922, there was a Chinese soccer team organized by students studying in Germany. Yu Bingquan was the captain, and Zhang Yulin and Tu Kaidi (Mr. Tu's elder brother) were important members of the team. Mr. Tu first showed his skills as a goalkeeper. In 1923, Zhang Yulin was the captain, and Tu served as an inside forward. In 1925, Tu was promoted to captain and also served as a center back. From that year until 1927, the team was at its peak and competed with local agricultural, industrial, commercial, and Berlin universities. Although there were wins and losses, the strength was strong and had become an undeniable fact. Unfortunately, in 1928, many of the team's strong players returned home one after another, and the team gradually stopped without support. In early 1923, Mr. Tu joined the SC Charlottenburg soccer team, which had more than 20 years of history. It was one of more than 20 sports associations in Berlin. Soccer was divided into adult, child, and student groups, each with seven teams, for a total of 21 teams. They competed once a week. The association also hired experts to provide training. The training methods were very adaptable, with one type focusing on endurance, such as cross-country running, and another type focusing on short-distance sprinting and various gymnastics. Training was held twice a week in the evening on the green field under electric light, regardless of wind or rain. Different countries have different tactics for soccer. England uses the M formation, the Soviet Union uses short passes, and Germany mostly adopts the English style, with offense and defense complementing each other, and the east, west, left, and right sides never stop for a moment. The center forward and the two wings are stationed in the enemy's camp, ready for impact. The German soccer season is popular all year round except for August. The daily expenses of the sports association rely on the income from soccer and track and field tickets in August. The treatment of players by the sports association is scientific, with no excessive or insufficient bias. After this legitimate training, Mr. Tu became strong and skillful. In 1924, Mr. Tu was promoted from the D team to the C and B teams. In 1925, he was selected to the A team as one of the forwards, opening a new record for Chinese people in the German soccer world. At that time, Mr. Tu also served as the center back of the A team in the school (University of Berlin). From 1926 to 1927, he won the Berlin University Championship for two consecutive years and the National University Championship for two years. In 1928, due to graduation examinations, he rarely participated. From 1929 to 1930, he also served the association in his spare time during his internship. This autumn, he plans to serve his country, and this gentleman's skills will be seen on the green field.

Many Talented People in the Tennis World 122

Many students studying in Germany like tennis very much. There are large-scale competitions in spring and autumn, and the skills are improving and talented people are emerging. Mr. Tu is also one of the best among them. According to his account, there is Luo Guangcai from Sichuan, a giant in the German world. His left and right strokes are as he wishes. His high and low shots are powerful and unusual. His future achievements are immeasurable. He once defeated the first-class German talents Wolf and Yaeuicke. These two had defeated the Filipino Aragaon when he visited the country. From this, it can be seen that Luo's skills are superb. At the same time, there is also Liu Jing, whom the French call the Chinese Borotra, one of the four French musketeers. He is good at netsmanship. Liu's fame also comes from his constant activity on the net. Liu once lost to Luo by six to three, five to seven, and four to six. The skills of the two are very close. Last year, there was a Chinese tennis traveling team organized by students studying abroad. The team had six members: Luo Guangcai, Liu Jing, Tu Kaiyuan, Luo Guanggui, Xu Yuanyu, and Zhou Guanjun. They went through five or six cities and won every battle, returning with honors. Generally speaking, the tennis activities of students studying in Germany are on the rise.

German Sports Emphasize Universality 123

German sports emphasize universality. The goal is to develop all the people equally and not to focus on one or two special talents. Therefore, there is no exceptional treatment. Gymnastics has become an important part of every family. Among ball sports, soccer is the most developed, followed by tennis. Basketball and baseball are almost extinct. Track and field is strongly promoted. This is a national hobby that has been cultivated over decades, and there will probably be no major changes in the next ten years.

Free Talk

Words of Wisdom 124

— Hu Furen

The music of the natural world, like the crowing of roosters, the barking of dogs, the chirping of birds, and the buzzing of insects, is something people in cities can never enjoy.

Humans are the most intelligent of all creatures, and therefore suffer the most pain. Is this the price of intelligence?

The joy of reunion after a long separation is as different from the pain of separation as heaven is from earth.

There is no truly beautiful and virtuous woman in this world, nor is there a truly ugly and evil woman.

In stubborn families, parents-in-law hope that their daughters will have harmonious relationships with their husbands after marriage, but they do not want their own sons to be too attached to their wives. Is this the reason why there are so many troubles in old-fashioned families?

The pain of separation by death is the same as the pain of separation by distance; there is no need to distinguish which is lighter or heavier.

To live is to serve, not to enjoy. If everyone understands this, they can reduce many troubles.

A beautiful woman's heart is not necessarily good, and an ugly woman's heart is not necessarily evil. It is a great mistake for people to judge by appearance.

The coldness and warmth of human relationships and the fickleness of the world are excellent lessons for young people.

People's hearts are different, each with its own face. It is always difficult to find someone who truly understands you among all people.

There is nothing inherently wrong in the world; it is fools who create their own troubles. It can be seen that people in this world are the most ominous of all things.

A Record of National Martial Arts 125

— Song Lu

When I was a child studying in the county elementary school, there was a tea server named Old Zhang. He was already approaching sixty, but his spirit was vigorous, and he looked like he was only in his forties. During his free time, he liked to tease the students, often instructing them to strike his limbs with bamboo and wooden sticks. Old Zhang would raise his hands to receive the blows without suffering any harm. When he saw us practicing gymnastics, he would say, "This is the new-style boxing technique. However, practitioners only focus on form and not on substance, far inferior to boxing." Occasionally, when asked to demonstrate his skills, he could invert himself and climb a pillar, then slowly curl his body, advancing and retreating like a snake. One night, a thief broke in. Old Zhang, upon awakening, leaped onto the roof, captured the thief, and descended. His body was as light as a swallow. Upon closer inspection, it turned out to be his disciple. He scolded him, "I taught you a meager skill, and you use it to become a thief? I am poor and old, yet I am willing to end my days as a servant. You are too unworthy, ruining my reputation!" He then whipped him severely and let him go. Old Zhang soon passed away, and those who knew him mourned him.

Zhang Zhaojiu of Huizhou was a famous boxing master, skilled in internal strength, with techniques such as bone contraction and light body, capable of walking on water without wetting his shoes. He had many disciples, all of whom possessed unique skills. His son and grandson were also skilled in martial arts. Unfortunately, his family rules were not strict, so many of his disciples became thieves and bandits. His son was particularly strong and powerful, once visiting various iron shops and bending each instrument with one finger, instilling fear in everyone. Later, he fought with a monk and was killed by the monk's pressure point technique. From then on, his disciples slightly restrained themselves. Those who continued to commit acts of violence were mostly arrested by the authorities. Now, Zhang has long passed away, and his grandson is also over ninety years old, but he is honest, simple, humble, and courteous, not inferior to ancient gentlemen. To practice martial arts is to strengthen the body, and to possess skills is to defend oneself. It is not something to rely on to run rampant in one's village. A single thought can make one a chivalrous hero, and a single thought can harm oneself. I hope those who practice this will take this warning to heart.

A Record of Boating on West Lake Under the Moon 126

— Xiao Die

With Xiao Jian Xunmei, we stepped out of West Lake and planned to buy a boat to float on the Three Pools Reflecting the Moon. The bright moon had just risen, and the water reflected the moonlight, creating a clear and bright expanse. Several small boats came and went in the moonlit water, where even the smallest details were visible. I heard a faint flute sound rising from a boat, then suddenly stopping. Someone called out, "Yang Ziqing's Qing!" So we boarded Qing's boat together. Gazing into the distance, North Mountain and the East Market seemed to sleep under a veil of green gauze. I couldn't see buildings, only the lights reflected on the water, and the lotus leaves were smaller than a goose's eye. A faint fragrance wafted in the wind. Leaning on the oars in the middle of the stream, I played with the bright moon, gazing at the dustless jade palace and leisurely drifting on the golden waves. It was as if I were in a small crystal box, and all worldly realms were gone. Qing said, "This is paintable!" I grabbed a brush to write, but felt that my thoughts were elusive, coming and going without a trace. I felt desolate and empty, wanting to leave but then stopping again. When I returned to record it, it still didn't seem right. For the scenery that everyone in the world can see, not everyone can see it in the moment. When I hold a brush to write this scenery, it is also not necessarily the same as the scenery I saw at that moment. As Gu Foying's poem says, "Looking at the mountain and writing poetry are actually unrelated. If you happen to get a good line, it's not necessarily the true essence of the mountain, but it has captured my heart."

Women of Xuzhou 127

— Wan Cheng

The other day, the Commercial Press held a joyful banquet at Yizhixiang for the delegation from the Eastern Provinces Special Zone and the principals and teachers of secondary schools from various regions who led students to Shanghai for a visit. During the banquet, Chairman He Bingsong invited Ms. Yu Shiru, the principal of Xuzhou Girls' Middle School, to speak.

Ms. Yu first described the general situation of girls' education in Xuzhou, then spoke about the character and physical appearance of Xuzhou women. She said that Xuzhou women were straightforward, loyal, and steadfast in character, but their physical appearance was rougher, darker, and fatter than that of southern women.

Ms. Yu's pronunciation was clear, and her words were concise and to the point. She is truly an outstanding talent in the women's world.

Exquisite Anecdotes of Jade Rice 128

— Zheng Yimei

"Food is the first necessity of the people" is a famous saying of our ancestors. Steaming grains into rice began with the Yellow Emperor, as seen in the "Jijia Zhou Shu." Since then, it has been passed down to this day without interruption. Rice grains are divided into japonica and glutinous rice. Farmers sell them to shops, and the shops always grind, roll, and mix them with polishing powder, employing various outdated methods that cannot be broken. My friend, Mr. Zhang Erxin, a Bachelor of Science in Physics from Soochow University, has discovered through research that rice naturally contains acidity. The more external the layer, the stronger the acidic reaction, and the most abundant the vitamins. Grinding and rolling will lose its vitality and digestive aids, and mixing with polishing powder will make it impure and difficult to clean, which is harmful to the stomach and intestines. Therefore, Mr. Zhang has invented a kind of healthy rice using scientific methods. Under the guidance of Dr. Xue Wenyi, a medical doctor from the University, and Mr. Yuan Pilie, a Master of Engineering from Cornell University, who is responsible for the manufacturing, a shop has been established on Heng Street in Fengmen, Suzhou, with a sign that reads "Wanyuan," providing healthy rice to meet the needs of society. This rice retains its original color, and can be cooked and eaten without washing, and its swelling properties are extremely strong. It can also treat beriberi, stomach ailments, and physical weakness. Recently, a public demonstration was held at the Free Farmers' Market, where County Magistrate Huang Yunzhen personally delivered a wonderful speech, briefly stating that eating healthy rice simply means encouraging people to eat more bran and chaff, but it should not be misunderstood as teaching people to be pigs. Although healthy rice contains bran and chaff, it is not coarse and is very palatable. The listeners laughed heartily. Mr. Fei Shuwe, a famous pedantic recluse in Suzhou, never eats rice from the market and specially entrusts villagers to buy rice that is pounded using traditional methods, taking the unhusked grain. When eating, he mixes it with bran and cooks it. Now that he has obtained healthy rice and tried cooking and eating it, he praises it endlessly, saying that it has the merits of color, aroma, and taste all in one.

Barber Competition 129

— Meng Lin

Recently, a barber competition was held in central New York. As a result, Bao'er Dase of Courtland Village defeated Manchu of Waterloo Village. However, Manchu was not convinced because he was already a sixty-six-year-old barber, so he recently wrote a letter to Bao'er Daseller, thirty-nine years old, requesting a second competition with him.

The conditions are that this competition will have a quota of thirty heads, ten heads will be cut using electric clippers, ten heads will be cut using ordinary hand-held clippers, and the last ten heads will be limited to using scissors. Furthermore, no one is allowed to stand within six feet of the barber chair during the competition to avoid hindering movement. The judges must be unrelated to the competitors either directly or indirectly.

According to Manchu himself, the reason for his last failure was entirely because the electric clippers were not working smoothly when cutting the first head. As for the hand-held clippers, he has been using them for forty-eight years, so of course he is very skilled.

Manchu mostly used scissors to cut, occasionally switching to hand-held clippers. As a result, Manchu shaved nineteen heads in one hour, fifty-one minutes, and five seconds, while Bao'er Dase cut twenty-three heads.

Speaking of records, Manchu's fastest time for a male head is two minutes and thirty-five seconds, while Bao'er Dase's is two minutes and fifty seconds. As for a female head, he only needs three minutes, while Bao'er Dase's fastest time is four minutes and thirteen seconds. No wonder the old man refuses to accept defeat.

Tragedy 130

— Yun Gong

Once, I visited a nunnery in Wumen and saw a young nun participating in the Dharma seat. The sound of the bells and chimes evoked a strange feeling in me. I thought that she must have unspeakable hidden pain, so she sought the door of silence and extinction. Later, the old nun told me that she was actually the daughter of a prominent family in Yushan. Due to a momentary error, she was seduced by a wild man, and after experiencing hardship, she eventually fell into disgrace and was expelled from her family and rejected by her hometown. So she came here to shave her head and repent. When the old nun spoke, the young nun also faintly heard it, and tears filled her eyes, as if her sad and resentful thoughts were stirred up. I couldn't bear it and hurriedly left, feeling dejected. Afterwards, whenever I passed this nunnery, it seemed as if an unfinished tragedy was still intermittently reflected in my mind, causing me to feel sad and unable to stop myself.

Later, I came to Shanghai and became quite fond of movies. I never liked Clara Bow and others who advocated licentiousness, but I was particularly moved by Lilyan Tashman's sadness. From the film "Self-Made Wife" to "The Vengeance," I was deeply touched. The characters played by Lilyan were often ill-fated women. Their origins were bitter ("The Love Thief"), and their endings were desolate ("The Lone Wolf's Daughter"). I thought of the young nun in Wuxia. If I were to write a script and have Lilyan perform it, it would surely make all the sentimental people in the world cry together.

In domestic films, there are not many tragedies with power. However, I was deeply surprised by the depth of feeling in the Tianyi Film Company's "Tears of the Empty Door." The changes in the plot and the strangeness of the background seem to put the viewer in the snow and sea of the Arctic Ocean. Although frightened and horrified, one cannot help but feel a sense of desolation. Chen Yumei's performance as the protagonist is particularly outstanding. Her tears fall like pearls, and her sorrow is profound. I would like to call her the Lilyan Tashman of the East. The result of the film's events is reminiscent of what I saw in the nunnery in Wuxia, which makes me feel that the situation is real and the power to move people is even deeper. In ancient times, people who sold laughter for a thousand pieces of gold were foolish. In the vast world, only genuine tears are precious.

A Trip Around the Yellow Sea (26) 131

— Huang Yanpei

So, what should we do then? Let me offer some suggestions, but first, I want to clarify that my words are addressed to the average Chinese person, not to a specific person or group.

First, build up your physical fitness. This is the root of everything. I can honestly say that every time I return to my country from abroad, the biggest shock is the sight of our compatriots coming and going on the streets. Half of them look like ghosts! How can they be compared with the people of any other country? Living a life of peace for ten thousand days at most allows people to ridicule you, which is not a big deal. But when the country is in trouble and lives are at stake, those who have been trained and those who have not are vastly different. Thinking of this, I want to say that the greatest enemy of our country for ten thousand years is opium, and the greatest sinners are those who profit from opium from top to bottom. These people are not only the harbingers of national demise, but also the executioners of our race.

Speaking of building up physical fitness, how should we proceed? Everyone must practice individually, and every region must practice. The government must also establish a policy and formulate various laws and regulations to ensure that the whole country makes continuous efforts at the same time. This is not just about training a few athletes to show off at sports meets. We should focus on universal and basic physical training. Look at Japan, where every school has kendo and judo for their students, but absolutely none for Korean students. On the one hand, they emphasize basic training, and on the other hand, they don't want them to train. Which side do we Chinese people want to learn from? What kind of methods does our government use to treat our own young men and women?

Second, firmly believe in science. For more than a hundred years, the opening up of the mysteries of the universe, the expansion of the effectiveness of all things, and the improvement of human life have all been due to science. If the world had no ships, trains, airplanes, telegraphs, telephones, electricity, various machines, as well as guns, ammunition, submarines, tanks, etc., how much different would Europe and the United States be from us, and where would the great powers' strength lie? We must not think that other people's inventions and creations allow us to "sit back and enjoy the benefits." We can travel on other people's ships on the sea and communicate through other people's wires under the sea. We must know that for the past fifty years, tens of millions and hundreds of millions of dollars have flowed out of the country, leaving the people poor and the country depleted, all because of the idea of "sitting back and enjoying the benefits."

Speaking Society

Three Eras (1) 132

— Zhang Henshui

(1) Under the Baton

Nongshangbu Street was a relatively neat alley. A row of tall locust trees with lush green foliage lined the stone-paved road, reflecting the white-plastered walls of the houses on both sides. The green was green, and the white was white, which was really pleasing to the eye. The sun was shining directly on the treetops, scattering a green shade all over the ground. A hawker selling sour plum soup was resting in the shade. In front was a wooden tray with many small bowls, supporting an enamel basin filled with ice cubes. Behind was a wooden bucket filled with a jar of sour plum soup. In the middle was a carrying pole. The hawker selling sour plum soup held it, first saying, "Drink it!" Then he started singing, "Osmanthus sugar is added a lot, sweet and delicious to drink!" After singing, he added, "Drink it!" Zhang Xiaosan, a rickshaw puller, had just pulled a long trip from the east city and earned fifty cents. He dragged the rickshaw with his right hand and used a blue cloth towel in his left hand to wipe the sweat from his head, slowly walking in the shade of the trees. He heard the hawker selling sour plum soup shouting and looked at the sparkling water blocks in the basin. He felt a coolness drill into his throat. He couldn't help but put down the rickshaw and asked, "One cent for two bowls? Give me a big scoop with more ice!" The hawker selling sour plum soup didn't say a word, took a small bowl, and opened the lid of the jar, using a wine scoop to scoop two scoops of sour plum soup. He grabbed a few pieces of crushed ice and put them in the bowl. Zhang Xiaosan said, "More, more!" The hawker selling sour plum soup glanced at him and smiled faintly, "More ice is also money, bought it." He put the bowl on the wooden tray. Zhang Xiaosan picked up the small bowl and gulped it down in two sounds without taking a breath, drinking the sour plum soup clean. Only a few small pieces of ice were left at the bottom of the bowl. He simply poured the ice into his mouth, chewing it like beans, and handed the bowl to the hawker selling sour plum soup to scoop again. He drank until the third bowl when a big red door opened on the south side of the road, and a boy of seven or eight years old and a lady in her twenties came out, probably to look at the street.

Grain Prices in the Lower River Area are Stagnant 142

At Xinzha yesterday, rice shipments from various groups in the northern Shanghai market were still surging, totaling thirty to forty ships. Sales in this street were extremely stagnant. Both high-quality and second-quality japonica rice fell by 0.2 yuan. Buying interest was extremely quiet. Market sentiment was generally loosening, so the situation was quite thin. Although there was not much early-season rice, its consumption was very sluggish, and prices also fell. Due to the abundance of japonica rice, imported round-grain rice was weak, falling by 0.1 yuan. Baopu round-grain rice was stagnant and did not move, with no distinction between honor and disgrace. For glutinous rice, the top grade from the old mortar was visibly weak but invisibly weakened. Discounts below the middle grade were significant enough. Liquor merchants' sales were unsatisfactory. There were about two hundred ships stored in the lower river area, totaling about thirty thousand stones of rice.

In the southern Shanghai rice market, the number of people at the early morning market was sparse. Top-grade rice from Changshu and Wuxi was stable. Ordinary middle-grade rice fell by 0.2 yuan. Sales of high-quality japonica rice from Suzhou, Tongzhou, Pinghu, and Lihai became even more sluggish, falling by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. Shipments of early-season rice from Nangang, Qingjiao, Songjiang, Fengxian, etc., arrived in abundance, but sales were stagnant, and there was still inventory. Opening prices for each product were lower by one to two tenths of a yuan. Zero sales of imported round-grain rice from Ye Xie and Zhang Yan were still acceptable, with an average situation turning weak. Sales of parboiled rice were slightly brisk, with tea and snack shops showing slight movement and a stable situation. There were about thirty ships arriving on the inner road, with each cargo totaling three to four hundred dan.

The Huangpu Iron Bridge Problem 155

The draft contract and explanatory statement have been submitted to the Municipal Government. The Huangpu Iron Bridge is being prepared by Yao Jizhong, Xu Qingwen, Gong Zhengfang, etc. to promote public welfare as a people-owned public undertaking, which will substantially assist the development of the Shanghai Municipal Government's transportation and commerce. Key central figures Zhang Jingjiang and Shanghai's business community Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Wang Binyan, Du Yuesheng, Yuan Ludeng, etc. have all provided support. However, the progress of the construction has not been active in recent months. In order to show concern for municipal construction, a reporter from the New Voice Society visited Yao Jizhong, one of the bridge's initiators. As Yao was out on business, the reporter instead visited Gong Zhengfang to inquire about the bridge's construction plans and progress. According to Gong, the reason for planning to build this bridge was purely for the purpose of municipal transportation to meet the needs of the development of the Pudong City. Therefore, Yao was extremely enthusiastic about this planning. He signed a draft contract with the German Meng Aen Bridge Company on February 27. As Yao considered this matter to be of great importance, he has not yet submitted this draft contract to the Municipal Government for approval. Now that the National Congress has resolved that the state has a policy to encourage people-owned public works, it has now been decided to actively proceed. Yesterday, the contract was submitted to the Municipal Government for review. The original document is as follows:

Draft Contract: This contract was signed on February 16, the 20th year of the Republic of China, in Shanghai. The two signing parties are Yao Jizhong, Xu Qingwen, Shen Yuren, hereinafter referred to as the conveners, and the China branch of the German Meng Aen Company, hereinafter referred to as the company. Now that the conveners intend to build a steel pontoon bridge across the Huangpu River, passing through Dongjiadu in Nantou, Shanghai City, to Dongjiadu in Pudong, the company is willing to build the bridge and provide all materials. The matters agreed upon by both parties are listed below: Article 1: Matters to be handled by the company 1. Build a steel pontoon bridge from Dongjiadu in Nantou, Shanghai City, to Dongjiadu in Pudong Wharf. The capacity of the surface quality is as follows: (A) One tram road (B) Two car roads (C) Two pedestrian roads The above totals 46 feet wide, listed separately (A) Tram road 18 feet (B) Car road 16 feet (C) Pedestrian road 12 feet 2. The estimated value of the bridge and wharf management rooms mentioned in the previous article shall not exceed US$1 million, which shall be verified and determined after measurement. (3 This Contract) shall be delivered on the date of signing, with detailed instructions for bridge construction, and the complete plan and drawings shall be provided on the date of signing the formal contract. The Construction Division shall be responsible for the construction, which shall be completed within 24 months from the date of signing the formal contract, except in case of unforeseen events and strikes. (4) The company guarantees that the bridge is suitable for use and can meet the conveners' complete expectations. The guarantee period shall be at least five years, and proper storage shall be ensured during the period, which shall be the responsibility of the conveners (this clause refers to repairs). Article 2: Matters to be handled by the conveners (1) After submitting the instructions and obtaining approval from the government, a formal contract shall be signed immediately. (2) The bridge price shall be temporarily set at US$1 million, which shall be repaid every six months according to the amount of income. The first payment shall be calculated from the date of completion and handover to the conveners. (3) The outstanding amount of this bridge price shall be subject to an annual interest rate of 8%, calculated from the date of handover of the bridge to the conveners. (4) The conveners shall fulfill the guarantee agreed upon in Article 2 of this clause by a bank approved by the company (Supplementary Items) If the company fails to complete the construction within the stipulated time in the contract, except for matters related to Article 1, Item 3, it shall compensate for the loss, and the conveners may reduce the price by 2%. If the delay exceeds one month, the reduction shall be increased by another 2%, and the same shall be done for subsequent delays on a monthly basis. If the company's bridge construction materials have arrived in Shanghai and the conveners suspend the progress of the project due to an accident, the company shall also be compensated for the loss, and the annual interest rate shall be priced at 8% of the value of the materials and the time elapsed. To have evidence, both parties signed on the above-mentioned date to ensure good faith. Signatures: Kang Daofu, Ge Leke, Yao Jizhong, Shen Ziren, Xu Qingwen. Witness: Gong Zhengfang.

Bridge Construction Instructions: The instructions for the Shanghai Pudong Bridge construction plan are hereby explained as follows: (1) The length of the bridge is 1,200 feet (2) The width of the bridge is 46 feet (3) The middle of the bridge is equipped with a tram track that is 18 feet wide. The space on both sides of the track is 16 feet wide and is available for various vehicles to travel back and forth, including cars, trucks, horse-drawn carriages, and handcarts. In addition, there are sidewalks on both sides, each 6 feet wide (4) The load capacity of the bridge is about 350 tons for each 130 feet section (5) There are many ships in the port area, not only naval warships, huge merchant ships, and sailing ships traveling back and forth. The opening of the bridge shall be built according to the necessary width (6) The movable section of the bridge is rotated by an iron chain at the fixed section. The extended section extends to the floating boats at both ends. The outer poles of the floating boats are equipped with Dyce engines. When the bridge is opened, the movable section is pushed open to 180 degrees by the force of the spiral propulsion. The opening width is 213 feet (7) To defend against significant collisions by passing ships, the bridge is equipped with sufficient and powerful defenses (8) The highest point of the bridge from each section to the water surface is 18 feet to 20 feet. Small boats can pass under the bridge (9) The cost of the bridge is US$1 million. Signature: Kang Daofu, Ge Leke, representatives of Meng Aen Company.

The Yangtze River Shipping Industry is in a Slump 156

Lack of Imports and Exports

The Yangtze River shipping industry can now be said to have declined to the extreme, with a lack of imports and exports and the suspension of Chinese steamships. Yesterday, a reporter met with a key figure in the shipping industry who told the truth about the decline. It is recorded as follows:

Jiangxi Goods Blocked: Since the Communist Party’s disturbances in Jiangxi, only two or so of the province’s eighty-one counties have been spared from the bandit disaster. The transportation of goods along the Nanxun Road has recently been commandeered by the army to suppress bandits, causing small boats and barges in the inland rivers to be used for official purposes. This has caused the accumulation of goods in Ganzhou without ships to transport them, which has prevented the largest exports of summer cloth, porcelain, paper, miscellaneous grains, etc. from being transported out. The purchasing power of society has weakened and there are fewer goods going to Shanghai. Jiujiang Port, which used to be the number one port for Yangtze River freight transport, now has no cargo on both incoming and outgoing ships.

Dageng Tungsten Halts: The Dagengling tungsten mine in Jiangxi Province is world-renowned. The amount of this mineral sand purchased and exported by Britain, Germany, and other countries each year is often 200,000 to 300,000 tons, with each ton worth 300 to 400 yuan, which is a great source of profit for Jiangxi Province. It has not been restored since it was suspended by bandits last year. Dageng has already been recovered by the National Army, but the miners have not yet been gathered to mine. As a result, not a single bag of tungsten ore has been shipped out this year.

Hunan and Hubei Goods are Severely Lacking: Since the Pinghan Railway has been opened to traffic, goods have accumulated along the line due to a lack of cars and obstructions. Other large commodities have not been able to be transported. Shaanxi and Gansu goods have been diverted to the Longhai Railway and shipped by Haizhou ships. In Hunan Province, the Xiangxi waterway is still completely impassable, resulting in no incoming goods. It can be said that the upstream shipping industry is hopeless. Only Anhui tea in the downstream is slightly transported to Shanghai.

Seagoing Vessels Travel the Yangtze River: Many Chinese river boats have been off duty since May 17. Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company temporarily transferred the seagoing vessel "Fairness" to travel the Yangtze River to meet the needs of passengers. The vast ships that have been idle for a long time can be dispatched to travel the Yangtze River during this flood season to recover the lost freight. It can also resist the increase in foreign ships. The ship's workers will make a request.

British Merchants Increase New Ships: Two new Yangtze River ships ordered by Taikoo Dockyard last year are new types of fast ships with diesel engines. One is called Wuhu, which has already set sail, and the other is called Wuxue, which has also been completed. It has a deadweight of 2,938 tons. Taking advantage of the time when Chinese ships are all stopped, it has been telegraphed to Shanghai to formally

Yesterday Afternoon, National Products Emporium Sealed Off 157

Amusement Section Issue

The Bureau of Works Considers it Disobedience

Gongshang She Says the China National Products United Emporium Shut Down After Relocating from Freedom City Hall to New World for Over Half a Month; Yesterday Afternoon, it Suddenly Ceased Operations, Leading to Various Rumors. A Reporter from Gongshang She Believing This Matter Greatly Impacts the Future of National Products, Personally Investigated and Learned the Facts Were Due to a Misunderstanding. The Interview Details Are Recorded Below:

Reason for Closure: After the emporium took over the entire New World building, it used a portion of Freedom Hall as the emporium, with the rest remaining as the amusement section. However, according to the Bureau of Works regulations, amusement venues require a license. Since the emporium had changed its name and management, the previous New World license was no longer valid, and the emporium was instructed to obtain a new license. The emporium complied, but due to certain internal facilities not meeting the regulations, personnel from the Bureau of Works' Engineering and Sanitation departments inspected the premises and informed the emporium manager that improvements must be made within one week. Only after a re-inspection confirming the improvements would the license be issued. After one week, inspectors found the improvements still incomplete and granted a final extension of forty-eight hours. Yesterday, three days past the forty-eight-hour deadline, the required improvements remained unfinished. The Bureau of Works considered this intentional defiance and ordered the responsible police station to send officers to enforce closure. This is the reason for the emporium's closure.

Circumstances of Closure: Around 2 PM yesterday, the responsible police station dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to execute the order. Manager Zhang Zilian and others were in Pudong participating in the Du Ancestral Hall ceremony, and no one was available to liaise. The detectives immediately ordered the iron gates closed, ceasing operations. Several hundred people had already purchased tickets and entered. To maintain credibility, the emporium continued with various amusements until 6 PM when it closed, and visitors were released through a side door. Some visitors inside were unaware the gates had been closed.

Merchants' Meeting: The participating merchants in the emporium originally had a united association. Upon witnessing the situation, they convened an emergency meeting. They collectively believed the emporium and amusement section were separate entities and questioned who would bear the responsibility for the emporium's losses due to the amusement section's lack of a license. A decision was made to send representatives to negotiate with the general office to minimize losses for the merchants.

Emporium Notice: Around 5 PM, a notice was posted at the emporium entrance, stating: "(This emporium is operating as usual but was unexpectedly sealed off by the police station this afternoon at 3 PM without cause. Serious negotiations are underway. Special announcement.)" As of the time of this report, the issue remains unresolved.

Emporium Announcement: China National Products United Emporium Urgent Announcement: Our emporium moved from Nanjing Road to No. 4 Jing'an Temple Road on May 5th and has been operating as usual. Unexpectedly, on June 9th at 3 PM, the British Concession police station sent officers to order a shutdown, sealing all doors of the emporium and deploying officers to monitor and prevent entry and exit. (Omission) Apart from separately telegraphing the Central Party Headquarters, National Government, Executive Yuan, Ministry of Industry, Ministry of Foreign Affairs for serious negotiations, and telegraphing various provincial and municipal party headquarters, governments, chambers of commerce, and agricultural, labor, and student groups, taxpayer Chinese associations, etc., for united assistance, this is a special announcement.

Land in the City Center Will Soon Be Available for Claiming 164

Five Features of the Land Available for Claiming

To promote the prosperity of the city center area and encourage citizens to engage in construction in the area, the municipal government has decided to make available one of the most valuable parts of the land it has acquired. The area is bounded by Sanmin Road to the north, Xiangyin Road to the south, Songhu Road to the east, and the city center administrative area to the west, totaling approximately 800 mu. It will be offered at the original cost, without markup, only adding a proportionate share of the road construction and other construction costs. It is divided into two grades, Grade A at 2,500 yuan per mu and Grade B at 2,000 yuan. The location is quiet and convenient for transportation, making it very suitable for commercial and residential use. The Land Bureau has announced that the period from June 21st to July 20th will be the:

Priority return period for original landowners. After July 20th, the official claiming period will begin, and anyone can go to claim land. The procedures are extremely simple. Here are some of the features of this claiming offer: (1) Excellent Location: The center of this offering is a large park with an area of over 300 mu. The terrain is flat, and the air is fresh. Once landscaped, the surrounding area will easily become the most beautiful residential area in the city. To the east is the city center administrative area, where all agencies and public buildings are concentrated, adding to its appeal. (2) Convenient Transportation: Xiangyin Road is an important thoroughfare from Jungong Road to Jiangwan. The land available for claiming is located next to this road. Newly built roads include Qimei Road, Songhu Road, Sanmin Road, etc. Previously, travel from Shanghai mainly followed the West Sports Club Road. With the completion of Qimei Road, this is now the only shortcut. Currently, public buses run on both West Sports Club Road and Xiangyin Road, making transportation very convenient. People in Shanghai who are unfamiliar with the city center area believe it must be very far from the city. However, in reality, the distance from the Bund on Nanjing Road in the public concession to Fanwangdu Park is the same as the distance from the Bund to the city center area. Therefore, even in terms of distance from the current market, its location is exceptionally convenient. (3) Low Land Prices: Currently, land prices in the Jiangwan Xiangyin Road area average 1,200 to 1,300 yuan per mu, and the roads are still cinder roads, the drainage facilities are still incomplete, and the supply of water and electricity is the same. Now, the land price for the land that the municipal government is claiming includes the road and drainage construction costs. Grade A land costs only 2,500 yuan per mu, and Grade B land costs only 2,000 yuan per mu. The municipal government will use all the land prices collected in the shortest period of time to build the area's drainage system, asphalt roads, and other facilities. Consider that the price of land next to a cinder road with no facilities already requires 1,200 to 1,300 yuan. Now, the land price per mu next to a fully equipped asphalt road is only 2,000 to 2,500 yuan. Is this not extremely low? (4) Favorable Measures: The low land prices available for claiming have already been described. In addition, there are regulations to exempt house taxes and transfer taxes within three years. It is also well known that the general public mentality is largely unwilling to make large-scale investments in places where land prices are low. Therefore, 10% (residential area) to 20% (commercial area) is used to show flexibility. The City Works Bureau has also offered prizes to solicit house designs, selecting the best of several types and publishing them as a collection for citizens to use as a reference for construction. (5) Comprehensive Facilities: The roads within this claiming area are generally planned to be built with asphalt surfaces, with drainage ditches below to facilitate the discharge of rainwater and sewage. Maintaining quietness within the residential area is the top priority, reducing the passage of vehicles and planting more trees to make the entire area a park. Currently, there is an electric line set up by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company on Songhu Road, and there is also a water pipe of the company under the road. In the future, it will be very convenient to build roads in this area and connect the pipes. At the corner of Songhu Road and Xiangyin Road, the municipal government also plans to build a police station to maintain the area's security. As for post offices, schools, banks, and shops, they will all arise as needed.

Decision Made to Use One Bale of Silk and Two Carts as a Unit

Lawyers Association Requests Revocation of the Shanghai Public Safety Bureau's Notice Banning Rent Arrears 167

After the Shanghai Lawyers Association was notified of the Shanghai Public Safety Bureau's Notice No. 25 regarding banning rent arrears issued in October of the 19th year of the Republic of China, Commissioner Yu Zhongluo proposed a recommendation stating that this matter conflicts with the Civil Procedure Law and divides judicial power. The matter was already decided by the council to

Page 14

submit a petition to the Judicial Yuan and the Ministry of Judicial Administration for approval to order the revocation. A letter was sent to the municipal government, but there has been no response for months. Therefore, the association submitted the matter to the 80th Joint Meeting of Executive and Supervisory Committees and resolved to submit another petition to the Executive Yuan, requesting the Shanghai municipal government to order the Shanghai Public Safety Bureau to revoke the notice banning rent arrears to uphold the rule of law. The original text is copied below. Petition for Ordering the Shanghai Municipal Government to Revoke the Public Safety Bureau's Notice Banning Rent Arrears to Uphold the Rule of Law. The temporary Civil Procedure Regulations approved by the National Government stipulate in Article 2, Paragraph 1 that disputes between landlords and tenants should be under the jurisdiction of the primary court. Article 1 of the Civil Procedure Law promulgated by the National Government states that civil litigation is under the jurisdiction of the court where the defendant's ordinary trial registration is located. When a tenant owes rent and the landlord requests payment, it is entirely a civil case that should naturally be under the jurisdiction of the court where the ordinary trial registration is located. Article 8 and Article 13 of the Municipal Organization Law state that the municipal government's handling of affairs and issuance of regulations must not conflict with central laws. In October of the 19th year of the Republic of China, because the association's Shanghai Public Safety Bureau issued Notice No. 25 regarding banning rent arrears, which stated that in the future, any rent arrears would be strictly dealt with without leniency once reported by the landlord. The council decided that rent disputes fall exclusively under the jurisdiction of the courts, and the Public Safety Bureau has no right to interfere. A letter was sent to the municipal government requesting a restraint. At the same time, a suggestion was made to the Judicial Yuan requesting the Shanghai District Court to vigorously implement provisional execution and other preservation procedures for rent arrears cases to prevent delays and escapes, and to allow rent recovery until the end of the execution to take both sides into consideration. Ministry of Justice No. 1002 replied that the suggestions have been notified to the Shanghai District Court. However, for several months, tenants have been subjected to police orders to pay or hand over rent due to rent arrears. On April 30th of this year, the association received a letter from a tenant in Yixing Lane on Guoqing Road seeking justice and decided to send a letter to the municipal government requesting detailed information on the specific measures for banning rent arrears. But both letters were not answered. Now, the association's 80th Joint Meeting of Executive and Supervisory Committees has decided that the Civil Procedure Regulations and the Municipal Government Organization Law, the Public Safety Bureau's Notice No. 25 issued in the 19th year of the Republic of China is not legally effective. If the court's judgment on the same rent arrears case conflicts with the Public Safety Bureau's punishment or differs, the court's judgment should prevail. At the same time, to respect the municipal government's intention to protect the landlord, we request the court to vigorously implement provisional execution and other preservation procedures to reconcile judicial and political parties. In addition to sending another letter to the municipal government to quickly revoke the Shanghai Public Safety Bureau's Notice No. 25 banning rent arrears, we also notify all landlords to file a lawsuit with the court if they encounter rent arrears and not to make any requests to the Public Safety Bureau. Sincerely presenting this petition to the Executive Yuan for review and approval to order the Shanghai municipal government to revoke the Public Safety Bureau's Notice Banning Rent Arrears to uphold the rule of law. Respectfully submitted to President Jiang of the Executive Yuan, Shanghai Lawyers Association Standing Committee respectfully presents.

City Chamber of Commerce Cables Request to Stop Tax on Zhejiang Province Cocoon Industry 168

The City Chamber of Commerce cabled the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, stating: "On the 8th of this month, we received a letter from the Silk Factory Association stating that the Association previously considered the proposed taxation of the silk cocoon industry in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hubei to be inconsistent with the taxation standards set by the ministry and requested the National Government's Ministry of Finance to quickly correct it. We also sent a letter to your association requesting your support and forwarding it to the case. On the 3rd of this month, we received your letter No. 1216, which copied the Ministry of Finance's letter No. 6414. We have already ordered the Finance Departments of the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hubei to deliberate and respond. The Shanghai Silk Factory Association's request to exempt the cocoon industry from business tax, etc., has arrived at the Ministry, and we will order them to comply with the response after the Finance Department's response arrives. This reply, etc., is forwarded to your association. We also received a telegram from the Ministry of Finance with the same meaning. Although the translation of the telegram does not explicitly show rejection, it clearly recognizes that this request is reasonable. Unexpectedly, on the 4th of this month, we received the approval from the Zhejiang Finance Department, which misinterpreted the Ministry's text and disrupted the administrative system in violation of central regulations. Therefore, we wrote another article describing the Zhejiang Finance Department's approval and requested the Ministry of Finance to strictly prohibit it. Therefore, we copied the draft and sent it to your association for assistance and telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to order the Zhejiang Finance Department to stop collecting taxes. The Zhejiang Finance Department's approval of the Silk Factory Association's document states that the business tax is taxed on business, and anyone who has a business transaction, whether buying or selling, must pay the business tax. Cocoon merchants collecting cocoons is a business, so they cannot be exempted from the obligation to pay taxes. The cocoon posting certificate issued by the cocoon firm is charged according to the stove and has a special permit nature and is different from the intermediary certificate, etc. The meaning of the approval is divided into two levels. The first level is that the business tax must be paid regardless of whether it is buying or selling. This level is completely contrary to the approval of the Ministry, which only buys and does not sell and has no business income. Villagers are not taxed for business. Regardless of the type of business, selling is the business, so only buying and not selling proves that the business has not been completed. According to the views of the Zhejiang Finance Department, if there is a tax on buying and a tax on selling, a business can collect two business taxes. This is clearly inconsistent with the facts. Therefore, this point alone is enough to prove that the cocoon collection of silk factories in the mainland is the nature of villagers, and there is no reason to pay taxes according to the previous approval of the Ministry. Its interpretation of the cocoon posting certificate as a special permit business and different from the intermediary certificate is even more a misinterpretation of the Ministry's text. In our country, before the general business tax was handled, the so-called intermediary tax, slaughter tax, etc. were taxed because they had a special business nature. This time, the tax on the special business tax that was charged in the past is changed to the newly set name, all to avoid miscellaneous taxes. Therefore, the shops that collect the special business tax will no longer collect the general business tax as a consistent principle of the Ministry. Moreover, Article 11 of the Supplementary Measures has the same taxes as other business taxes, whether it is charged according to the stove or not, the nature is the same as the business tax, and it should not be taxed repeatedly. The Zhejiang Finance Department's approval failed to appreciate the Ministry's regulations and should be ordered to stop collecting taxes. Sincerely, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Decree from the Department Ordering the Organization of a Factory Supervision Committee 173

The Shanghai County Government yesterday received an order from the Department of Civil Affairs, stating that it was acting in accordance with Instruction No. 92, Min Zi, of the Ministry of Interior. The instruction stated that it had received a consultation from the Ministry of Industry regarding the transfer of documents from the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce to the Ministry of Railways concerning the organization of a factory supervision committee to resolve labor-capital disputes. After a general meeting, it was decided that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, in conjunction with relevant ministries, should deliberate and handle the matter, and the record was kept on file. Labor-capital disputes are a major obstacle to the future of industry. If labor-capital problems are not resolved, there will be no hope for the revitalization of industry. In recent years, many factories in the country have been forced to shut down due to labor-capital disputes. If guidance and supervision are not provided, the consequences are unimaginable. The proposals in the case were pertinent and to the point. In order to promote cooperation between labor and capital and the development of industry, the Ministry has submitted for promulgation the Factory Law and the Factory Inspection Law, and is now preparing to implement them in order. At the beginning of implementation, it is essential to understand the management and economic situation of each factory, so that future measures will have a basis. The welfare of labor must be improved, but the funds for improving labor welfare mostly come from the increase in production rates, and the increase in production efficiency depends on the scientific management of factories. We are hereby copying the original case for your review. The first step is to investigate the management and economic situation of each factory, and then, based on economic principles and the best management methods, to formulate improvement standards. This is a matter of great importance, and you are requested to instruct your subordinates to fill in the attached form in detail and report back for verification and forwarding. The county magistrate is instructed to follow the instructions and instruct his subordinates to fill in the attached form in detail and report back for verification and forwarding. This decree now presents the original proposal for organizing a factory supervision committee to resolve labor disputes as follows: The country is flooded with foreign goods. All daily necessities such as clothing, food, housing, and transportation, such as foreign cloth, felt, wool, rice, noodles, canned goods, foreign pine oil, paint, railway materials, cars, and gasoline, are imported from foreign countries, resulting in a daily decrease in cash and a difficult life for the people. If this is not changed, how can the country be built? The reason is that Chinese workers only know how to increase wages and do not seek to improve efficiency. Capital only knows how to exploit and hire low-wage workers in order to obtain more dividends, and fails to take into account the improvement of workers' lives and treatment. Therefore, although there are abundant raw materials, abundant capital, and a large number of workers, labor and capital cannot fully cooperate, and the future of industry is still without hope for development. In order to promote production and increase the national economy, it is proposed that the central government organize a factory supervision committee, and hire factory management experts, factory accounting experts, factory efficiency experts, and legal experts to guide and supervise all matters of each factory. The first step is to investigate the management and economic situation of each factory, and then, based on economic principles and the best management methods, to formulate improvement standards. The second step is to stipulate appropriate distribution of workers' living expenses, capital interest rates, and bonuses for both labor and capital. If the factory management is improper or the workers' treatment is poor, an immediate order should be issued to improve it. Labor should prioritize efficiency and should not arbitrarily demand extra conditions or threaten to strike. The principle of equality and mutual benefit between labor and capital should be sought to achieve cooperation. As a result, both parties can perform their duties and production will increase day by day, the economy will become more prosperous, and industrial development can compete with the great powers. Is it not only a passive resistance?

Wage Increase Issue for Employees of British-Owned Gas Company Remains Unresolved 175

Decision Awaits Board Meeting

The Chinese employees of the British-owned gas company in this city have requested a wage increase because the company has increased the wages of foreign employees by as much as 40 to 50 percent, while Chinese employees have not received any increase. However, the company has repeatedly made excuses to delay. Here is a summary of various reports heard yesterday:

Labor Negotiations: Over the past two days, the labor side sent Bao Yugen, Yao Liankun, and two others as plenipotentiary representatives to meet with Chief Engineer Baker at the factory's writing room for consultation. The initial meeting yielded no results because the capital side firmly refused to increase wages.

Further Negotiations: The two representatives, Bao and Yao, feeling that they had not achieved their goals, had no choice but to return to report. After further discussions, the labor side felt that both the Chinese and foreign departments were employees of the factory and should be treated equally without discrimination. How could they favor one over the other? This was truly unfair. Therefore, more than ten department heads from each department, including Zhu Deyu, Zhu Wenyao, Chai Bende, Lu Zhengrong, Wu Qigui, Zhou Maotou, Lu Afa, Lou Maosheng, Su Jinlin, and Dong Shunyi, accompanied Bao and Yao to negotiate again. After much hesitation, the factory finally replied that the issue of the wage increase would be decided at the board meeting on the 11th. This matter cannot be resolved for the time being and a response will be given after the meeting. The workers then withdrew. The outcome remains to be seen after the board meeting.

Factory's Explanation: According to the factory's statement to the Nichinichi Shimbun reporter, there are two reasons for the wage increase for foreign employees: (1) The price of gold has skyrocketed. Foreign employees in China convert their wages from Chinese currency to gold pounds, so the Chinese currency must be increased. However, although the increase is nominal, there is no actual increase when calculated in gold pounds. (2) Foreign employees have high expenses and their standard of living is higher than that of Chinese employees. Therefore, a small child economic assistance allowance is recently given as a child rearing fee. However, the labor side believes that both of these reasons are unreasonable. Regarding the first point, the impact of the rise in the price of gold not only affects foreign employees, but also affects Chinese employees. Regarding the second point, although the standard of living of foreigners is high, their salary level is already much higher than that of Chinese employees. Moreover, Chinese also have small children and should they not also receive small child economic assistance allowances? Therefore, the labor side still demands to achieve the goal of a wage increase.

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Government and Court Demanding Strict Crackdown on Security Guards 176

Guaranteeing Personal Freedom of Chinese

The Shanghai Ratepayers Association of Chinese residents yesterday sent a letter to the Municipal Government and the Special District Court, requesting a strict crackdown on security guards arbitrarily detaining people. The letter stated, "Respectfully, according to a letter from Mr. Dai Chengxiang, it was reported on the 3rd of this month that Portuguese national Tersa claimed to be the director of the security guards and that the defendants were detectives investigating matters in the association. If someone is to be detained, he must issue a detention warrant. We are deeply shocked to read this. Personal freedom should be respected. Therefore, Article 8, Paragraph 1, of the Provisional Constitution of the Tutelage Period of the Republic of China stipulates that people shall not be arrested, detained, interrogated, or punished except in accordance with the law. According to the current Criminal Procedure Law, except for current offenders who may be arrested without a warrant by anyone, other defendants may not be arrested by private individuals. Only prosecutors, presiding judges, or judges appointed by the court who believe that the conditions for legal detention are met may issue a detention warrant. The Shanghai Detective Security Association is organized by private individuals. How can they issue detention warrants to detain people? Now, Portuguese national Tersa openly claims in our country's court that he has the power to issue detention warrants, which is a contempt for our country's sovereignty. If this is not strictly prohibited, unscrupulous foreigners will arbitrarily issue detention warrants in the name of detective security associations to detain people, and our country's sovereignty will be completely destroyed. The freedom of our Chinese people will be trampled upon. The harm is even worse than consular jurisdiction. Therefore, we hereby request your association to quickly discuss with Chinese and foreign authorities to severely warn the Shanghai Detective Security Association not to issue detention warrants to detain people. If they dare to violate the law, the association will be dissolved and the perpetrators will be punished to the fullest extent of the law in order to protect national rights and respect freedom." The association believes that the issues raised in the letter regarding sovereignty and freedom are very important and should be forwarded to the relevant authorities. We respectfully request that you investigate, strictly crack down, and maintain national sovereignty and the freedom of the people. This is respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Shanghai Special District Court.

Lawsuit Proceeding for Victims of the "Xinkang" Ship Disaster 178

Few Family Members Remain Untraced

Advertisements Published to Notify Them

The Xinkang Ship Disaster Victims Association held a committee meeting yesterday afternoon. First, Standing Committee member Mr. Zhu reported on the progress of all association affairs and the consultations with legal advisors Wu Jingxiong and Sheng Zhenwei. Then, the issue of the lawsuit was discussed. All procedures have been prepared by lawyers Wu and Sheng. It was pointed out that because there are many victims' families, their origins are different. After the disaster, because the case has not been resolved, some have returned to their hometowns, some are in remote villages, some have moved elsewhere, and some have sought a living elsewhere. While most of those who are still in or near Shanghai have sent letters requesting progress or have come in person to discuss association affairs, some victims' families remain untraced. The lawyers require individual letters of authorization from all victims' families to represent them in the lawsuit. Currently, while more than half of the families have signed letters of authorization, a small number of families have not yet completed this procedure due to relocation, so the lawyers have not submitted the lawsuit in order to protect the interests of all. However, the statutory period for the lawsuit is about to expire, so it is necessary to proceed as quickly as possible to avoid self-inflicted delays. After discussion, the committee decided to immediately publish advertisements in various newspapers, giving families living outside of Shanghai or who have relocated three weeks to come to the association to report and prepare to sign letters of authorization to the lawyers in order to achieve success and avoid unnecessary losses. Other procedural matters were discussed before the meeting adjourned.

Anti-Drug Association Urges Smokers to Enter Hospitals for Addiction Treatment 179

Prescribing Guarantee Measures

Requesting Introduction from Various Organizations

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association yesterday sent a letter to various organizations stating, "Respectfully, this association has investigated the situation of smokers and found that most of them smoke due to illness, especially those who are poor and helpless. If measures are not taken to quit as soon as possible, they will sink into the abyss and will never be able to extricate themselves. This association, based on its resources, has specially negotiated with appropriate hospitals to provide various semi-free and completely free methods in order to fundamentally treat and relieve the suffering of smokers. More than 260 smokers have been introduced to hospitals by this association, all of whom voluntarily quit their addiction and will never smoke again. However, recently, the hospitals have stated that after the smokers arrive at the hospital, the doctors treat them according to the severity of their addiction, prescribing the amount of medication and the length of treatment. While many follow the hospital rules and quit their addiction, quite a few are lazy and unmotivated, giving up halfway. This not only undoes the previous efforts but also wastes a considerable amount of medical expenses, which is very regrettable. They have requested that this association find a way to remedy the situation. Since the smokers have already resolved to quit their addiction, they should not give up halfway. If this lazy nature is not changed and measures are not taken to supervise them, not only will the hospitals be unwilling to continue to accept them, but this association will also find it difficult to introduce them again. Therefore, it is now stipulated that all smokers who are determined to quit smoking should be introduced by organizations or guaranteed by shops. Smokers can only enjoy free treatment if they enter the hospital to quit smoking and are willing to comply with hospital regulations until their addiction is completely cured. They must not give up halfway. With such meticulous restrictions and supervision, the results will be significant. Accordingly, we are sending this letter for your information. In the future, if there are smokers who request to quit smoking, we hope that your association will introduce them to this association and help them find a reliable guarantor so that the smokers will not give up halfway and waste their efforts. The smokers will be fortunate, and this association will be fortunate."

In addition, the weather was beautiful, with the rising sun shining brightly, adding to the brilliance of the fresh flowers and rare herbs. The various ranks followed in order, proceeding south on Rue Way Kong to Avenue Li Mei, turning east onto Quai de Montigny, then south on Route Cardinal Mercier, and further east on Laobei Men Street, and finally on Xiaodong Men Street all the way to the Jinliyuan Wharf. The crowds of onlookers along the way were immense, praising it as unprecedented.

The Grand Parade Yesterday (Photo by this newspaper) 184

Inside the Du Ancestral Hall 185

The Wharf Scene: Several paifang (ceremonial gateways) were erected at Jinliyuan Wharf.

Members of the security regiment were stationed at the wharf to maintain order. From 9:00 a.m. to 11:00 a.m., cars arrived in an endless stream, and male and female guests flocked to the wharf to board the prepared steamships to await departure. At 11:30 a.m., the parade arrived at the wharf. A shout of joy and the sound of firecrackers echoed each other. The military police, regiments, and various school boy scouts boarded the ships one by one in an orderly manner. A special steamship was also prepared for female guests. As the ships were anchored one after another, the sound of firecrackers grew louder. The various military bands took turns playing in the ships, and the boy scouts also sang happily. The music and songs were magnificent, an unprecedented spectacle in the Huangpu River.

The Scene at Gaoqiao: After an hour's voyage, the ships arrived at Gaoqiao, Pudong, where the clean wharf and lush trees were a refreshing sight. Male and female guests disembarked one after another and were guided by reception staff to the Du Ancestral Hall either by car or on foot, all feeling infinitely interested. Gaoqiao, bordering the river and the sea, is a strategic location with beautiful scenery along the way. The crowds of onlookers on the roadside were like a grand festival.

A Glimpse of the Du Ancestral Hall: A five-story, extremely large painted archway was erected in front of the Du Ancestral Hall. The ancestral hall has five rooms and three courtyards. The second courtyard is the main hall, and the third courtyard is the place where the ancestral tablet is enshrined. Two majestic stone lions stand in front of the gate, which is grand and spacious. Various gifts from all walks of life are displayed in each room, numbering in the thousands, a dazzling array of beauty. Due to the large number of guests, more than a hundred straw sheds were built around the ancestral hall. The hall's opera stage was also a straw shed to the west of the ancestral hall, which was unusually large and could accommodate more than two hundred tables. However, there were more than 10,000 guests yesterday afternoon, who could not all be accommodated at once, so they had to be accommodated in two or three shifts. The crowded and lively scene was truly rare. It is expected that there will be even more guests today, the main day of the ceremony.

Male and Female Guests: About 10,000 male and female guests arrived yesterday, including male guests such as Yang Xiaotian, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Yuan Ludeng, Qian Jieshen, and Yu Ziying, and female guests such as Zheng Yuxiu, Mrs. Wang Liangchou, and Mrs. Yang Zhaoyun.

Enshrinement: Yesterday was the procession across the river, while the enshrinement ceremony will be held at 5:00 a.m. today (the 10th). Most of the thousands of guests yesterday did not return to Shanghai, preparing to attend the above ceremony.

Commemorative Postmark: The Postal Administration of this city, in order to commemorate the completion ceremony of the Du Ancestral Hall, specially set up a temporary post office on the spot, giving away commemorative envelopes and adding a commemorative postmark.

Chairman Congratulates: The Secretariat of the National Government yesterday sent a telegram to Yang Xiaotian, asking him to represent the government in congratulating Du Yuesheng. The original telegram said: "To Army Counselor Yang Xiaotian, Shanghai, the 10th of this month is the completion of Mr. Du Yuesheng's new ancestral hall. Please represent the government in offering congratulations. By order. Secretariat of the National Government, Qing."
